Q1. Which data structure is best for implementing LRU cache with O(1) operations?
A) Array + hash
B) Doubly linked list + hash map
C) Stack
D) Queue
Answer: B
Explanation: Doubly linked list + hash map; list maintains order, hash for O(1) access.

Q2. What is the worst-case time complexity of QuickSort (naïve pivot)?
A) O(n log n)
B) O(n^2)
C) O(n)
D) O(log n)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(n²) when pivot choices are poor (e.g., sorted input).

Q3. Which traversal of a BST yields sorted order?
A) Preorder
B) Inorder
C) Postorder
D) Level-order
Answer: B
Explanation: Inorder.

Q4. Which data structure supports Dijkstra’s algorithm most efficiently?
A) Simple array
B) Binary heap / priority queue
C) Linked list
D) Stack
Answer: B
Explanation: Binary heap (or Fibonacci heap for better amortized complexity).

Q5. Amortized complexity of push in dynamic array (doubling) is:
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(1)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: O(1) amortized.

Q6. Which is best for range minimum queries (static array)?
A) Segment tree
B) Hash table
C) Stack
D) Queue
Answer: A
Explanation: Segment tree or sparse table for static arrays.

Q7. Time complexity to find cycle in directed graph using DFS is:
A) O(V + E)
B) O(V^2)
C) O(E^2)
D) O(log V)
Answer: A
Explanation: O(V+E) via DFS and recursion stack.

Q8. Which sorting algorithm is stable?
A) QuickSort (standard)
B) Merge Sort
C) Heap Sort
D) Selection Sort
Answer: B
Explanation: Merge Sort is stable (if implemented accordingly).

Q9. Minimum number of comparisons to find both min and max from n elements (~ best known)?
A) 2n − 2
B) 3n/2 − 2
C) n log n
D) n
Answer: B
Explanation: ≈ 1.5n − 2 using pairwise comparisons.

Q10. Which structure is best for adjacency when the graph is dense?
A) Adjacency list
B) Adjacency matrix
C) Edge list always better
D) Heap
Answer: B
Explanation: Adjacency matrix is better for dense graphs (O(n^2) storage).

Q11. For which problem is dynamic programming appropriate?
A) Binary search
B) Overlapping subproblems & optimal substructure (e.g., knapsack)
C) Simple loops only
D) Sorting arrays
Answer: B
Explanation: DP for overlapping subproblems and optimal substructure.

Q12. Which heap supports decrease-key in O(1) amortized?
A) Binary heap
B) Fibonacci heap
C) Pairing heap
D) Unordered array
Answer: B
Explanation: Fibonacci heap (amortized).

Q13. Which algorithm finds MST for sparse graphs efficiently?
A) Prim with binary heap
B) Prim with adjacency matrix
C) Bubble Sort
D) DFS
Answer: A
Explanation: Prim + binary heap for sparse graphs.

Q14. What is the space complexity of recursion for DFS on depth d?
A) O(1)
B) O(d)
C) O(n) always
D) O(log n)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(recursion depth) = O(d).

Q15. Which hash collision resolution uses linked lists at buckets?
A) Linear probing
B) Chaining
C) Double hashing
D) Quadratic probing
Answer: B
Explanation: Chaining.

Q16. Which data structure is optimal for implementing a priority queue?
A) Unsorted array
B) Binary heap
C) Linked list stack
D) Binary search tree (balanced)
Answer: B
Explanation: Binary heap gives O(log n) insert/extract.

Q17. Longest Common Subsequence (LCS) is solved by:
A) Greedy
B) Dynamic Programming
C) Divide-and-Conquer only
D) Hashing
Answer: B
Explanation: DP.

Q18. Which is an online algorithm?
A) QuickSort
B) Insertion sort for streaming input
C) MergeSort
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Processing items as they arrive.

Q19. Complexity of building a heap from array (heapify) bottom-up:
A) O(n log n)
B) O(n)
C) O(log n)
D) O(n^2)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(n).

Q20. Which structure supports range sum queries with updates efficiently?
A) Fenwick tree (BIT) or Segment tree
B) Plain array only
C) Hash map only
D) Stack
Answer: A
Explanation: BIT or Segment tree.

Q21. Which algorithm finds articulation points in a graph?
A) Dijkstra
B) Tarjan’s DFS (low-links)
C) Kruskal
D) Bellman-Ford
Answer: B
Explanation: Tarjan-style low-link algorithm.

Q22. For topological sorting, which graph property is required?
A) Graph must be directed acyclic (DAG)
B) Graph must be undirected
C) Graph must be complete
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: DAG.

Q23. Which technique reduces constant factors in string search (Boyer–Moore)?
A) Backward scanning + bad-character/good-suffix heuristics
B) KMP only
C) Rabin-Karp only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Boyer–Moore heuristics skip characters.

Q24. KMP algorithm achieves pattern matching in:
A) O(n*m)
B) O(n + m)
C) O(n log m)
D) O(n^2)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(n + m).

Q25. Balanced BST with guaranteed log n height:
A) AVL or Red-Black tree
B) Simple BST always
C) Linked list
D) Heap
Answer: A
Explanation: AVL and Red-Black maintain height O(log n).

Q26. Which is used for disjoint set union optimizations?
A) Path compression + union by rank
B) Sorting only
C) BFS
D) Heap
Answer: A
Explanation: Path compression and union by rank.

Q27. Complexity of matrix multiplication naive is:
A) O(n^2)
B) O(n^3)
C) O(n log n)
D) O(n)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(n^3) naive.

Q28. Which algorithm uses greedy for single-source shortest path with negative edges allowed?
A) Dijkstra
B) Bellman–Ford
C) Floyd–Warshall
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Bellman–Ford handles negative edges (no negative cycles).

Q29. Which structure is best for undo functionality?
A) Queue
B) Stack
C) Tree
D) Heap
Answer: B
Explanation: Stack (LIFO).

Q30. Which sorting algorithm is in-place and unstable?
A) Merge sort
B) Quick sort
C) Bubble sort
D) Counting sort
Answer: B
Explanation: Quick sort is in-place but not stable.

Q31. What is height of binary heap with n nodes?
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(1)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(log n).

Q32. Which traversal prints nodes level by level?
A) Inorder
B) Preorder
C) Level-order (BFS)
D) Postorder
Answer: C
Explanation: Level-order.

Q33. Where is tail recursion optimized typically?
A) Languages/runtime that support tail-call optimization (e.g., some functional languages)
B) All languages always
C) Never
D) Only in hardware
Answer: A
Explanation: When TCO is supported.

Q34. Which algorithm uses divide-and-conquer for closest pair of points?
A) O(n^2) brute force
B) O(n log n) divide and conquer
C) O(log n) only
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Divide and conquer yields O(n log n).

Q35. Which operation on binary search tree is average O(log n)?
A) Search, insert, delete (if balanced)
B) None
C) All operations O(n) always
D) Only insert O(1)
Answer: A
Explanation: If balanced.

Q36. For union-find with m operations and n elements, complexity is approximately:
A) O(m α(n)) (α is inverse Ackermann)
B) O(m n)
C) O(n log n)
D) O(1) always
Answer: A
Explanation: Nearly linear with α(n) factor.

Q37. Which algorithm is best for all-pairs shortest path on dense graphs?
A) Dijkstra repeated
B) Floyd–Warshall
C) DFS
D) BFS
Answer: B
Explanation: Floyd–Warshall (O(n^3)) is simple for dense graphs.

Q38. Which data structure is suitable for implementing BFS frontier?
A) Stack
B) Queue
C) Heap
D) Hash map
Answer: B
Explanation: Queue.

Q39. Which algorithm finds max-flow in networks efficiently for many real-world graphs?
A) Ford–Fulkerson (Edmonds–Karp variant)
B) Dijkstra
C) Prim
D) Kruskal
Answer: A
Explanation: Edmonds–Karp (or Dinic, Push–relabel better in practice).

Q40. Which string hashing technique reduces collisions?
A) Rolling hash with mod large prime (Rabin–Karp)
B) No hashing
C) Simple sum of chars only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Rolling polynomial hash with mod.

Q41. Which algorithm is used to compute SCCs?
A) Dijkstra
B) Kosaraju / Tarjan
C) Prim
D) KMP
Answer: B
Explanation: Kosaraju/Tarjan.

Q42. For approximate nearest neighbor in high dimensions, commonly used technique:
A) KD-tree (good in low dims)
B) Locality Sensitive Hashing (LSH)
C) Simple scan always best
D) Binary heap
Answer: B
Explanation: LSH for high-dimensional ANN.

Q43. Which BSP (binary space partition) technique used in graphics also used conceptually in search?
A) kd-tree
B) Heap
C) Queue
D) Stack
Answer: A
Explanation: kd-tree for spatial partitioning.

Q44. Which algorithm is used for top-k queries in streaming data?
A) Reservoir sampling (for uniform sampling) or heap for top-k
B) Bubble sort
C) Merge sort only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Min-heap of size k for streaming top-k.

Q45. Which is true about stable matching (Gale–Shapley)?
A) Always finds a stable matching and is optimal for proposing side
B) May fail
C) Only works for even sets
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Gale–Shapley always finds stable matching, proposer-optimal.

Q46. Which of these is NOT a Coffman deadlock condition?
A) Mutual exclusion
B) Hold and wait
C) No preemption
D) Starvation
Answer: D
Explanation: Starvation is a symptom, not one of Coffman’s four.

Q47. Which scheduling algorithm is fair and preemptive with a time quantum?
A) FCFS
B) Round Robin
C) SJF non-preemptive
D) Priority without aging
Answer: B
Explanation: Round Robin.

Q48. Which page replacement approximates LRU but is more efficient?
A) FIFO
B) Clock (Second Chance)
C) Optimal
D) Random
Answer: B
Explanation: Clock algorithm approximates LRU.

Q49. Which kernel type runs most services in user space, minimal kernel?
A) Monolithic kernel
B) Microkernel
C) Hybrid kernel
D) Exokernel
Answer: B
Explanation: Microkernel.

Q50. IPC mechanism that uses producer-consumer buffers can use:
A) Shared memory + semaphores
B) Only files
C) Only signals
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Shared memory combined with semaphores.

Q51. Page fault occurs when:
A) Data is already in RAM
B) Accessed page not in main memory
C) CPU executes I/O only
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Page not present in memory.

Q52. Which isolation level allows dirty reads?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read
D) Serializable
Answer: A
Explanation: Read Uncommitted allows dirty reads.

Q53. Which is an example of non-preemptive scheduling?
A) Round Robin
B) FCFS (non-preemptive)
C) Shortest Remaining Time First
D) Preemptive priority scheduling
Answer: B
Explanation: FCFS can be non-preemptive.

Q54. In UNIX, which primitive blocks until child process terminates?
A) fork()
B) exec()
C) wait()/waitpid()
D) kill()
Answer: C
Explanation: wait()/waitpid().

Q55. Which is primary function of OS?
A) Manage hardware & provide services to applications
B) Only run user apps
C) Only compile code
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Resource management and abstraction.

Q56. Semaphore initialized to 1 is used as:
A) Binary semaphore / mutex
B) Counting semaphore only
C) Barrier only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Binary semaphore for mutual exclusion.

Q57. Thrashing is reduced by:
A) Increasing physical memory or reducing multiprogramming level
B) Adding more processes always
C) Reducing CPU speed
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: More RAM or fewer processes reduces thrashing.

Q58. Which memory allocation scheme divides physical memory into fixed-size frames?
A) Segmentation
B) Paging
C) Contiguous allocation
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Paging uses frames.

Q59. Which syscall changes the file descriptor into a new program in Unix?
A) fork()
B) exec()
C) open()
D) close()
Answer: B
Explanation: exec replaces process image.

Q60. Which method resolves deadlocks by prevention?
A) Banker's algorithm (avoidance)
B) Killing processes (detection & recovery)
C) Prevention by disallowing one Coffman condition
D) All of above
Answer: C
Explanation: Prevention removes one of the conditions (e.g., disallow hold-and-wait).

Q61. Which is true about user-level threads vs kernel-level threads?
A) User-level threads are faster to create but cannot utilize multiple CPUs unless kernel aware
B) Kernel-level threads are always slower and useless
C) Both same in behavior
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: User threads cheap but limited in multiprocessor usage.

Q62. Which file system metadata structure stores permissions, owner, and pointers?
A) inode (UNIX)
B) FAT table
C) Master boot record
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: inode holds metadata.

Q63. In a multi-level paging scheme, translation requires:
A) Multiple memory accesses for page table levels
B) Single access always
C) No memory access
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Each level requires an access unless cached (TLB).

Q64. Which isolation level gives full serializability?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Serializable
D) None
Answer: C
Explanation: Serializable ensures full serializability.

Q65. Which is a real-time scheduling algorithm for fixed priorities?
A) EDF (earliest deadline first) — dynamic
B) Rate Monotonic Scheduling — fixed priority
C) Round Robin only
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Rate monotonic is fixed-priority real-time algorithm.

Q66. Kernel preemption improves:
A) Latency for tasks in kernel mode
B) Throughput always
C) Disk speed only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Better responsiveness/latency.

Q67. Which structure holds process state, registers, and resource pointers?
A) PCB (Process Control Block)
B) File descriptor only
C) Kernel stack only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: PCB.

Q68. Virtual memory addresses are translated to physical addresses by:
A) MMU (Memory Management Unit) with page tables
B) CPU cache only
C) Disk only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: MMU with page tables & TLB.

Q69. Which technique avoids copy-on-write overhead?
A) Always copy on write
B) Remain with single writer or use efficient CoW mechanisms (question ambiguous)
C) Use proper OS support (kernel-level CoW is efficient)
D) None
Answer: C
Explanation: Kernel-level CoW reduces overhead by using copy only on modification.

Q70. Which measure is used to predict performance in multiprogramming?
A) CPU utilization
B) Only memory size
C) Only disk speed
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: CPU utilization, throughput, turnaround time, response time.

Q71. Page replacement algorithm that uses frequency is:
A) LRU
B) LFU (Least Frequently Used)
C) FIFO
D) Random
Answer: B
Explanation: LFU uses frequency counts.

Q72. Which is true about spinlocks?
A) Busy-wait lock used in multiprocessor environments when wait time small
B) Sleep lock better in all cases
C) Spinlocks work well in single-CPU systems
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Spinlocks for short critical sections on multi CPUs.

Q73. Which is a primary difference of microkernel vs monolithic kernel?
A) Microkernel moves many services to user space (smaller kernel)
B) Monolithic has no drivers
C) Microkernel is always slower without exception
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Microkernel keeps minimal services in kernel.

Q74. Which blocking I/O transfers control back to process immediately?
A) Blocking I/O waits; non-blocking returns immediately
B) Blocking always returns immediately
C) Both same
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Non-blocking returns immediately while blocking waits.

Q75. Which technique reduces TLB misses for multiple processes?
A) TLB shootdown overhead management and large pages / shared TLB entries
B) Increase I/O only
C) Reduce cache only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Use large pages or TLB flush optimizations to reduce misses.

Q76. Which normal form eliminates partial dependency?
A) 1NF
B) 2NF
C) 3NF
D) BCNF
Answer: B
Explanation: 2NF removes partial dependencies.

Q77. Which SQL clause is used to group rows?
A) WHERE
B) GROUP BY
C) ORDER BY
D) HAVING only
Answer: B
Explanation: GROUP BY groups; HAVING filters grouped results.

Q78. Which is true about indexes?
A) Always speed up writes
B) Speed reads, may slow writes and use space
C) No effect on queries
D) Always required
Answer: B
Explanation: Indexes speed reads but incur write overhead.

Q79. Which isolation level prevents lost updates and dirty reads?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read or Serializable (depends)
D) None
Answer: C
Explanation: Repeatable Read prevents non-repeatable reads; Serializable is strongest.

Q80. Which join returns matching rows plus unmatched from left table?
A) INNER JOIN
B) LEFT OUTER JOIN
C) RIGHT OUTER JOIN
D) FULL OUTER JOIN
Answer: B
Explanation: LEFT OUTER JOIN.

Q81. ACID property ensuring constraints are preserved:
A) Atomicity
B) Consistency
C) Isolation
D) Durability
Answer: B
Explanation: Consistency ensures DB constraints preserved.

Q82. What is normalization goal?
A) Reduce redundancy and update anomalies
B) Increase redundancy
C) Remove all data
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Reduce redundancy.

Q83. Which type of index is most suitable for equality searches?
A) Hash index
B) B-Tree index
C) R-Tree
D) Bitmap index only
Answer: A
Explanation: Hash index is optimal for equality; B-Tree for range.

Q84. A materialized view stores:
A) Query result physically for faster reads (needs refresh)
B) Nothing
C) Only SQL text
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Materialized views store results.

Q85. Which SQL command reclaims storage and reduces table size?

Explanation: VACUUM/OPTIMIZE.

Q86. Which concurrency control uses timestamps ordering to serialize transactions?

Q87. Which data model is document-oriented?

Explanation: Document DBs like MongoDB.

Q88. Which recovery technique uses WAL (Write-Ahead Logging)?

Explanation: WAL/ARIES ensures durability and recovery.

Q89. Which storage format helps columnar analytics?

Q90. Which SQL is DCL (Data Control Language)?

Q91. Which join is usually implemented using hash join in large datasets?

Q92. Which technique splits large tables across machines horizontally?

Q93. Which property is required for serializability?

Explanation: Serializability means equivalent to some serial order.

Q94. Which SQL clause filters groups after aggregation?

Q95. Which is best when writes are heavy and eventual consistency acceptable?

Q96. Which index type is beneficial for low-cardinality columns?

Q97. In a cluster, leader-based replication provides:

Q98. What is denormalization used for?

Q100. Which join algorithm benefits from both inputs sorted?

Q101. Which of the following is NOT an ACID property?

Q102. Which SQL statement creates a snapshot of the DB for backup?

Q125. Which protocol manages reliable file transfer?

C) O(n log n)

Answer: B
Explanation: O(n^3) naive.

Q28. Which algorithm uses greedy for single-source shortest path with negative edges allowed?
A) Dijkstra
B) Bellman–Ford
C) Floyd–Warshall
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Bellman–Ford handles negative edges (no negative cycles).

Q29. Which structure is best for undo functionality?
A) Queue
B) Stack
C) Tree
D) Heap
Answer: B
Explanation: Stack (LIFO).

Q30. Which sorting algorithm is in-place and unstable?
A) Merge sort
B) Quick sort
C) Bubble sort
D) Counting sort
Answer: B
Explanation: Quick sort is in-place but not stable.

Q31. What is height of binary heap with n nodes?
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(1)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: B
Explanation: O(log n).

Q32. Which traversal prints nodes level by level?
A) Inorder
B) Preorder
C) Level-order (BFS)
D) Postorder
Answer: C
Explanation: Level-order.

Q33. Where is tail recursion optimized typically?
A) Languages/runtime that support tail-call optimization (e.g., some functional languages)
B) All languages always
C) Never
D) Only in hardware
Answer: A
Explanation: When TCO is supported.

Q34. Which algorithm uses divide-and-conquer for closest pair of points?
A) O(n^2) brute force
B) O(n log n) divide and conquer
C) O(log n) only
D) None
Answer: B
Explanation: Divide and conquer yields O(n log n).

Q35. Which operation on binary search tree is average O(log n)?
A) Search, insert, delete (if balanced)
B) None
C) All operations O(n) always
D) Only insert O(1)
Answer: A
Explanation: If balanced.

Q36. For union-find with m operations and n elements, complexity is approximately:
A) O(m α(n)) (α is inverse Ackermann)
B) O(m n)
C) O(n log n)
D) O(1) always
Answer: A
Explanation: Nearly linear with α(n) factor.

Q37. Which algorithm is best for all-pairs shortest path on dense graphs?
A) Dijkstra repeated
B) Floyd–Warshall
C) DFS
D) BFS
Answer: B
Explanation: Floyd–Warshall (O(n^3)) is simple for dense graphs.

Q38. Which data structure is suitable for implementing BFS frontier?
A) Stack
B) Queue
C) Heap
D) Hash map
Answer: B
Explanation: Queue.

Q39. Which algorithm finds max-flow in networks efficiently for many real-world graphs?
A) Ford–Fulkerson (Edmonds–Karp variant)
B) Dijkstra
C) Prim
D) Kruskal
Answer: A
Explanation: Edmonds–Karp (or Dinic, Push–relabel better in practice).

Q40. Which string hashing technique reduces collisions?
A) Rolling hash with mod large prime (Rabin–Karp)
B) No hashing
C) Simple sum of chars only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Rolling polynomial hash with mod.

Q41. Which algorithm is used to compute SCCs?

B) Kosaraju / Tarjan
C) Prim
D) KMP
Answer: B
Explanation: Kosaraju/Tarjan.

Q42. For approximate nearest neighbor in high dimensions, commonly used technique:

B) Locality Sensitive Hashing (LSH)

D) Binary heap
Answer: B
Explanation: LSH for high-dimensional ANN.

Q43. Which BSP (binary space partition) technique used in graphics also used conceptually in search?

Answer: A
Explanation: kd-tree for spatial partitioning.

Q44. Which algorithm is used for top-k queries in streaming data?

B) Bubble sort
C) Merge sort only
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Min-heap of size k for streaming top-k.

Q45. Which is true about stable matching (Gale–Shapley)?
A) Always finds a stable matching and is optimal for proposing side
B) May fail
C) Only works for even sets
D) None
Answer: A
Explanation: Gale–Shapley always finds stable matching, proposer-optimal.

Q46. Which of these is NOT a Coffman deadlock condition?
A) Mutual exclusion
B) Hold and wait
C) No preemption
D) Starvation
Answer: D
Explanation: Starvation is a symptom, not one of Coffman’s four.

Q47. Which scheduling algorithm is fair and preemptive with a time quantum?
A) FCFS
B) Round Robin
C) SJF non-preemptive

Explanation: Round Robin.

Q48. Which page replacement approximates LRU but is more efficient?

B) Clock (Second Chance)

D) Random
Answer: B
Explanation: Clock algorithm approximates LRU.

Q49. Which kernel type runs most services in user space, minimal kernel?

B) Microkernel

Explanation: Microkernel.

Q50. IPC mechanism that uses producer-consumer buffers can use:

Answer: A
Explanation: Shared memory combined with semaphores.

Q51. Page fault occurs when:

Explanation: Page not present in memory.

Q52. Which isolation level allows dirty reads?

Explanation: Read Uncommitted allows dirty reads.

Q53. Which is an example of non-preemptive scheduling?

Answer: B
Explanation: FCFS can be non-preemptive.

Q54. In UNIX, which primitive blocks until child process terminates?

Q55. Which is primary function of OS?

Explanation: Resource management and abstraction.

Q56. Semaphore initialized to 1 is used as:

Explanation: Binary semaphore for mutual exclusion.

Q57. Thrashing is reduced by:

Explanation: More RAM or fewer processes reduces thrashing.

Q58. Which memory allocation scheme divides physical memory into fixed-size frames?

Q59. Which syscall changes the file descriptor into a new program in Unix?

Answer: B
Explanation: exec replaces process image.

Q60. Which method resolves deadlocks by prevention?
A) Banker's algorithm (avoidance)
B) Killing processes (detection & recovery)

D) All of above
Answer: C
Explanation: Prevention removes one of the conditions (e.g., disallow hold-and-wait).

Q61. Which is true about user-level threads vs kernel-level threads?

B) Kernel-level threads are always slower and useless

D) None

Explanation: User threads cheap but limited in multiprocessor usage.

Q62. Which file system metadata structure stores permissions, owner, and pointers?

Q63. In a multi-level paging scheme, translation requires:
A) Multiple memory accesses for page table levels

Explanation: Each level requires an access unless cached (TLB).

Q64. Which isolation level gives full serializability?

C) Serializable
D) None

Explanation: Serializable ensures full serializability.

Q65. Which is a real-time scheduling algorithm for fixed priorities?

Explanation: Rate monotonic is fixed-priority real-time algorithm.

Q66. Kernel preemption improves:
A) Latency for tasks in kernel mode

Explanation: Better responsiveness/latency.

Q67. Which structure holds process state, registers, and resource pointers?

Q68. Virtual memory addresses are translated to physical addresses by:

Explanation: MMU with page tables & TLB.

Q69. Which technique avoids copy-on-write overhead?
A) Always copy on write
B) Remain with single writer or use efficient CoW mechanisms (question ambiguous)
C) Use proper OS support (kernel-level CoW is efficient)
D) None
Answer: C
Explanation: Kernel-level CoW reduces overhead by using copy only on modification.

Q70. Which measure is used to predict performance in multiprogramming?

B) Only memory size

Answer: A
Explanation: CPU utilization, throughput, turnaround time, response time.

Q71. Page replacement algorithm that uses frequency is:

Answer: B
Explanation: LFU uses frequency counts.

Q72. Which is true about spinlocks?

Explanation: Spinlocks for short critical sections on multi CPUs.

Q73. Which is a primary difference of microkernel vs monolithic kernel?
A) Microkernel moves many services to user space (smaller kernel)

D) None

Explanation: Microkernel keeps minimal services in kernel.

Q74. Which blocking I/O transfers control back to process immediately?

B) Blocking always returns immediately

D) None

Explanation: Non-blocking returns immediately while blocking waits.

Q75. Which technique reduces TLB misses for multiple processes?

Explanation: Use large pages or TLB flush optimizations to reduce misses.

Q76. Which normal form eliminates partial dependency?

B) 2NF

Explanation: 2NF removes partial dependencies.

Q77. Which SQL clause is used to group rows?

B) GROUP BY

Explanation: GROUP BY groups; HAVING filters grouped results.

Q78. Which is true about indexes?
A) Always speed up writes
B) Speed reads, may slow writes and use space

D) Always required
Answer: B
Explanation: Indexes speed reads but incur write overhead.

Q79. Which isolation level prevents lost updates and dirty reads?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read or Serializable (depends)
D) None
Answer: C
Explanation: Repeatable Read prevents non-repeatable reads; Serializable is strongest.

Q80. Which join returns matching rows plus unmatched from left table?

Explanation: LEFT OUTER JOIN.

Q81. ACID property ensuring constraints are preserved:

Explanation: Consistency ensures DB constraints preserved.

Q82. What is normalization goal?

C) Remove all data

Explanation: Reduce redundancy.

Q83. Which type of index is most suitable for equality searches?

Explanation: Hash index is optimal for equality; B-Tree for range.

Q84. A materialized view stores:

Explanation: Materialized views store results.

Q86. Which concurrency control uses timestamps ordering to serialize transactions?

Q87. Which data model is document-oriented?

Explanation: Document DBs like MongoDB.

Q88. Which recovery technique uses WAL (Write-Ahead Logging)?

Q89. Which storage format helps columnar analytics?

Q90. Which SQL is DCL (Data Control Language)?

Q91. Which join is usually implemented using hash join in large datasets?

Explanation: Hash join.

Q92. Which technique splits large tables across machines horizontally?

Q93. Which property is required for serializability?

Explanation: Serializability means equivalent to some serial order.

Q94. Which SQL clause filters groups after aggregation?
A) WHERE
B) HAVING
C) ORDER BY
D) GROUP BY
Answer: B
Explanation: HAVING filters after GROUP BY.

Q95. Which is best when writes are heavy and eventual consistency acceptable?
A) Strongly consistent RDBMS only

Q96. Which index type is beneficial for low-cardinality columns?

Explanation: Bitmap indexes for low-cardinality columns.

Q97. In a cluster, leader-based replication provides:

Answer: A
Explanation: Leader/follower replication.

Q98. What is denormalization used for?

Q99. Which query plan metric matters most for optimizer?

Q100. Which join algorithm benefits from both inputs sorted?

Q153. Why are large pages (hugepages) used?

SET 1 (BEL)

Q2. What is the worst-case time complexity of QuickSort (naïve pivot)?

B) O(n^2)

D) O(log n)

D) Stack
Answer: B

Q53. Which is an example of non-preemptive scheduling?

C) Shortest Remaining Time First
D) Preemptive priority scheduling
Answer: B
Explanation: FCFS can be non-preemptive.

Q54. In UNIX, which primitive blocks until child process terminates?

SET 5 (BEL)

Q1. Which of the following is a key component of India's infrastructure development?
A) Space exploration
B) Deep-sea fishing
C) Mountaineering facilities
D) High-speed railways
Answer: D
Explanation: High-speed railways are a significant part of modern infrastructure projects aimed at improving connectivity and economic growth in India.

Q2. What is the primary goal of sustainable development?
A) Exploitation of natural resources to meet current needs
B) Rapid economic growth at any cost
C) Preservation of natural resources for future generations
D) Immediate improvement of living standards without considering environmental impact
Answer: C
Explanation: Sustainable development aims to meet present needs without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs, emphasizing resource preservation.

Q3. Which article of the Indian Constitution deals with Fundamental Duties?
A) Article 318
B) Article 48A
C) Article 390
D) Article 51A
Answer: D
Explanation: Article 51A, added by the 42nd Amendment, lists the Fundamental Duties of citizens in India.

Q4. Which of the following is a characteristic feature of the Animal Kingdom?
A) Cell walls made of cellulose
B) Autotrophic nutrition
C) Heterotrophic mode of nutrition
D) Presence of chloroplasts
Answer: C
Explanation: Animals are typically heterotrophic, meaning they obtain nutrients by consuming other organisms, unlike plants (autotrophic).

Q5. Which socio-religious reform movement in modern history aimed at eradicating social evils such as untouchability, caste discrimination, and promoting education and women's rights?
A) The Aligarh Movement
B) The Deoband Movement
C) The Brahmo Samaj
D) The Arya Samaj
Answer: C
Explanation: The Brahmo Samaj, founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy, was a prominent movement advocating for social reforms including abolition of Sati, caste discrimination, and promoting modern education.

Q6. Which of the following is a Constitutional Body in India?
A) Election Commission of India (ECI)
B) Planning Commission
C) National Investigation Agency (NIA)
D) Reserve Bank of India (RBI)
Answer: A
Explanation: The Election Commission of India is established under Article 324 of the Constitution, making it a Constitutional Body responsible for conducting elections.

Q7. What is the purpose of pasteurization in food processing?
A) To increase the nutritional content of food.
B) To enhance the colour of the food.
C) To add flavour to the food.
D) To destroy pathogenic microorganisms present in the food
Answer: D
Explanation: Pasteurization involves heating food (like milk) to a specific temperature for a set period to kill harmful bacteria and extend shelf life.

Q8. Which language is recognized as a Classical Language by the Government of India?

Q12. Which river is known as the "Dakshina Ganga" in India?

B) Yamuna
C) Godavari
D) Krishna

Explanation: The Godavari River is often referred to as the 'Dakshina Ganga' (Ganges of the South) due to its large size and extent, analogous to the Ganges in the north.

Q13. Which of the following letter will replace the question mark (?) in the given series? R, U, X, A, D, ?
A) G
B) H
C) F
D) I
Answer: A
Explanation: The pattern is +3 letters (R+3=U, U+3=X, X+3=A (wraps around Z), A+3=D, D+3=G).

Q14. Three Statements are given followed by two conclusions numbered I and II. Assuming the statements to be true, decide which conclusion(s) logically follow. Statement I: All fruits are vegetables. Statement II: Some vegetables are green. Statement III: Some green things are ugly. Conclusion I: Some vegetables are fruits. Conclusion II: Some green things are not ugly.
A) Both conclusions I and II follow
B) Only conclusion I follows
C) Neither conclusion I nor II follows
D) Only conclusion II follows
Answer: B
Explanation: From "All fruits are vegetables", we can infer "Some vegetables are fruits" (Conclusion I). Statement III "Some green things are ugly" does not necessarily imply "Some green things are not ugly" (Conclusion II is not definite).

Q15. Select the option that is related to the third number in the same way as the second number is related to the first number. 57:228 :: 79:?
A) 316
B) 341
C) 333
D) 329
Answer: A
Explanation: The relationship is ×4 (57 * 4 = 228). Therefore, 79 * 4 = 316.

Q16. If B denotes 'addition', C denotes 'division', and D denotes 'subtraction', then what will be the value of 12 D 4 C 2 B 3 = ?
A) 14
B) 13
C) 15
D) 12
Answer: B
Explanation: Substituting the symbols: 12 - 4 / 2 + 3 = 12 - 2 + 3 = 10 + 3 = 13.

Q17. Which two signs should be interchanged to make the given equation correct? 16 / 4 × 5 + 2 - 8 = 18
A) + and x
B) - and /
C) + and -
D) / and +
Answer: D
Explanation: Original: 16/4 * 5 + 2 - 8 = 4 * 5 + 2 - 8 = 20 + 2 - 8 = 14 (Incorrect). Interchange / and +: 16 + 4 * 5 / 2 - 8 = 16 + 20 / 2 - 8 = 16 + 10 - 8 = 26 - 8 = 18 (Correct).

Q18. Seven friends Alice, Bob, Carol, David, Eve, Frank, and Grace are sitting around a circular table facing the centre. Alice is immediate right of Bob. Bob and Carol are neighbours. Frank is between David and Eve. Grace is not next to Carol or Eve. Who is sitting between Alice and David?
A) Eve
B) Bob
C) Grace
D) Frank
Answer: C
Explanation: Arrangement: Bob-Alice-Grace-David-Frank-Eve-Carol. Grace sits between Alice and David.

Q19. Select the option that is related to the fifth word in the same way as the second word is related to the first word. KANGAROO: JOEY :: BEAR:?
A) Calf
B) Puppy
C) Chick
D) Cub
Answer: D
Explanation: A joey is a young kangaroo. A cub is a young bear.

Q20. Which of the following numbers will replace the question mark (?) in the given series? 14, 13, 15, 12, 16, 11, ?
A) 17
B) 16
C) 18
D) 15
Answer: A
Explanation: It's an alternating series. One series increases: 14, 15, 16, 17 (+1). The other decreases: 13, 12, 11 (-1). The next term is from the increasing series.

Q21. Rohan says, "Ajay's wife is the sister of my father's only son." How is Ajay related to Rohan?
A) Husband
B) Brother
C) Sister's husband
D) Mother's father
Answer: C
Explanation: "My father's only son" is Rohan himself. "Sister of Rohan" is Rohan's sister. "Ajay's wife is Rohan's sister". Therefore, Ajay is Rohan's sister's husband (Brother-in-law).

Q22. There are 133 boxes kept one above the other. What will be the position of the box from the bottom whose position from the top is 27th?
A) 139
B) 142
C) 123
D) 107
Answer: D
Explanation: Position from bottom = (Total number of boxes - Position from top) + 1 = (133 - 27) + 1 = 106 + 1 = 107.

Q23. Four letter-clusters have been given, out of which three are alike in some manner and one is different. Select the odd letter-cluster.
A) VWX
B) RSU
C) FGI
D) JKM
Answer: B
Explanation: VWX (+1, +1), FGI (+1, +2), JKM (+1, +2), RSU (+1, +2). VWX follows a different pattern.

Q24. Which of the following numbers will replace the question mark (?) in the given series? 1076, ?, 688, 494, 300, 106
A) 882
B) 872
C) 831
D) 858
Answer: A
Explanation: The difference between consecutive terms is decreasing: 688-494=194, 494-300=194, 300-106=194. The common difference seems constant. So, ? - 688 = 194 => ? = 688 + 194 = 882. And 1076 - 882 = 194.

Q25. In a certain code language, if RESCUE is coded as 'EUCRES' and HANDLE is coded as 'ELDHAN', then what will DANGER be coded as?
A) REGDAN
B) RGEDAN
C) REGADN
D) REGDND
Answer: A
Explanation: The word is divided into pairs of letters (RE SC UE) and the pairs are rearranged as (UE SC RE). DANGER -> (DA NG ER) -> (ER NG DA) -> ERNGDA. Let's recheck RESCUE -> EUCRES (swap last pair with first pair). HANDLE -> ELDHAN (swap last pair LE with first pair HA). DANGER -> ERNGDA. Ah, the pattern seems different. RESCUE (123456) -> EUCRES (563412). HANDLE (123456) -> ELDHAN (563412). DANGER (123456) -> RGEDAN (563412). So it's RGEDAN. Let's recheck the user provided answer A: REGDAN. RESCUE -> EUC RES (345 12?). No. Let's try pairs reversed: ER CS UE -> EUC SER. No. RESCUE -> E U C R E S. HANDLE -> E L D H A N. Pattern seems to be: Last letter, 2nd last, 3rd letter, 2nd letter, 4th letter, 1st letter? Let's try on DANGER: R E G A N D -> REGDND. This is option D. Let's try another pattern based on prompt's answer A: REGDAN. DANGER -> R E G D A N. Maybe: 6th, 5th, 3rd, 1st, 2nd, 4th? RESCUE -> E U C R S E. No. Let's assume the prompt's coding logic: RE SC UE -> EU CR ES. HA ND LE -> EL DH AN. DA NG ER -> ER GD AN. Option A REGDAN seems plausible if the middle pair remains in order: (ER) (NG) (DA) -> ERNGDA? Let's follow the first logic that matches option B: (123456) -> (563412). DANGER -> RGEDAN. Given the ambiguity, I'll stick with the provided answer A, assuming a different pattern: perhaps (DA NG ER) -> (ER)(NG)(DA) -> ERNGDA? Or (RE)(SC)(UE) -> (EU)(CR)(ES)? No. Let's assume a simple pair swap: 12 34 56 -> 56 34 12. DANGER -> ER NG DA. Let's assume the provided answer A is REGDAN, the pattern might be 6-5-3-1-2-4. RESCUE: E U C R S E. Not matching. Let's stick to the 563412 pattern which gives RGEDAN (Option B), but since the user provided answer A (REGDAN), I'll use that, acknowledging the pattern is unclear from the examples.

D) Postorder
Answer: C
Explanation: Level-order.

Q58. Where is tail recursion optimized typically?
A) Languages/runtime that support tail-call optimization (e.g., some functional languages)
B) All languages always
C) Never
D) Only in hardware
Answer: A
Explanation: When TCO is supported.

Q59. Which algorithm uses divide-and-conquer for closest pair of points?

Explanation: Divide and conquer yields O(n log n).

Q60. Which operation on binary search tree is average O(log n)?

D) Only insert O(1)

Q61. For union-find with m operations and n elements, complexity is approximately:

B) O(m n)
C) O(n log n)
D) O(1) always
Answer: A
Explanation: Nearly linear with α(n) factor.

Q62. Which algorithm is best for all-pairs shortest path on dense graphs?

Explanation: Floyd–Warshall (O(n^3)) is simple for dense graphs.

Q71. Which of these is NOT a Coffman deadlock condition?

Q9. Who is known as the 'Father of the Indian Constitution'?

Q10. The price of sugar is increased by 25%. By what percentage must a family reduce its consumption so as not to increase its expenditure?
A) 15%
B) 20%
C) 25%
D) 30%
Answer: B
Explanation: Let original price be 100, consumption 100. Expenditure = 10000. New price = 125. New consumption = x. 125x = 10000 => x = 80. Reduction = 20%.

Q11. A can do a piece of work in 10 days, while B can do it in 15 days. If they work together, how long will they take to complete the work?
A) 5 days
B) 6 days
C) 8 days
D) 9 days
Answer: B
Explanation: A's 1 day work = 1/10. B's 1 day work = 1/15. Together, 1 day work = 1/10 + 1/15 = 1/6. They will take 6 days.

Q12. A car covers a distance of 60 km in 1 hour 30 minutes. What is its speed in km/hr?
A) 30 km/hr
B) 40 km/hr
C) 45 km/hr
D) 50 km/hr
Answer: B
Explanation: Speed = Distance / Time = 60 km / 1.5 hours = 40 km/hr.

Q13. The average of 5 consecutive odd numbers is 21. What is the largest of these numbers?
A) 21
B) 23
C) 25
D) 27
Answer: C
Explanation: Let the numbers be x-4, x-2, x, x+2, x+4. The average is x, so x=21. The largest number is x+4 = 25.

Q14. A man buys a toy for Rs. 100 and sells it for Rs. 120. What is his gain percentage?
A) 10%
B) 15%
C) 20%
D) 25%
Answer: C
Explanation: Gain = 120 - 100 = 20. Gain % = (Gain / CP) * 100 = (20 / 100) * 100 = 20%.

Q15. What is the compound interest on Rs. 1000 for 2 years at 10% per annum, compounded annually?
A) Rs. 200
B) Rs. 210
C) Rs. 220
D) Rs. 110
Answer: B
Explanation: Amount = P(1 + R/100)^T = 1000(1 + 10/100)^2 = 1000 * (1.1)^2 = 1210. CI = 1210 - 1000 = 210.

Q16. The LCM of two numbers is 180 and their HCF is 6. If one of the numbers is 30, what is the other number?
A) 18
B) 24
C) 36
D) 45
Answer: C
Explanation: Product of two numbers = LCM * HCF. 30 * x = 180 * 6. x = 36.

Q17. If 30% of A is equal to 50% of B, what is the ratio of A to B?
A) 3:5
B) 5:3
C) 2:3
D) 3:2
Answer: B
Explanation: 0.30 * A = 0.50 * B => 3A = 5B => A/B = 5/3.

Q18. Find the missing number in the series: 5, 11, 23, 47,?
A) 95
B) 96
C) 97
D) 98
Answer: A
Explanation: The pattern is * 2 + 1. 47 * 2 + 1 = 95.

Q19. If 'CAT' is coded as 'DBU', how is 'DOG' coded?
A) EPH
B) FPI
C) EOH
D) FOH
Answer: A
Explanation: Each letter is shifted forward by one position. D -> E, O -> P, G -> H.

Q20. Pointing to a woman, a man says, "She is the daughter of the only child of my grandmother." How is the woman related to the man?
A) Sister
B) Mother
C) Aunt
D) Daughter
Answer: A
Explanation: "Only child of my grandmother" is the man's father. "Daughter of my father" is his sister.

Q21. A man walks 5 km East, then turns right and walks 3 km, then turns left and walks 2 km. In which direction is he from the starting point?
A) North-East
B) South-West
C) South-East
D) North-West
Answer: C
Explanation: He is 7 km East and 3 km South of the start, which is the South-East direction.

Q22. Find the odd one out: January, May, July, September.

Q25. If 'A' is 1, 'B' is 2, and so on, and 'BAT' = 23, what is 'CAT'?

Q31. In the context of a binary search tree (BST), which traversal method yields the elements in sorted order?
A) Pre-order
B) Post-order
C) In-order
D) Level-order

Q32. What is the maximum number of nodes in a binary tree of height 'h'? (Assume root is at height 0)
A) 2^h - 1
B) 2^(h+1) - 1
C) 2^h
D) 2^(h-1)
Answer: B
[cite_start]Explanation: A perfect binary tree of height h has 2^(h+1) - 1 nodes. [cite: 33]

Q33. Which of the following is not a property of a B-Tree?
A) All leaves are at the same level.
B) All nodes except the root have at least m/2 children.
C) The root has at least two children unless it is a leaf.
D) All nodes must be at least half-full, including the root.
Answer: D
[cite_start]Explanation: The root node of a B-Tree is an exception and can have fewer than half-full children (it must have at least 2 unless it is a leaf). [cite: 35]

Q34. The worst-case time complexity of the Quick Sort algorithm is:
A) O(n)
B) O(n log n)
C) O(n^2)
D) O(log n)
Answer: C
[cite_start]Explanation: The worst-case for Quick Sort occurs when the pivot element is always the smallest or largest element, leading to an unbalanced partition and a complexity of O(n^2). [cite: 36]

Q35. Dijkstra's algorithm is used to find:
A) The minimum spanning tree
B) The shortest path from a single source in a weighted graph
C) The transitive closure of a graph
D) The strongly connected components of a graph
Answer: B
[cite_start]Explanation: Dijkstra's algorithm finds the shortest paths from a single source vertex to all other vertices in a graph with non-negative edge weights. [cite: 37]

Q36. Which algorithm design technique is used in finding the minimum spanning tree using Kruskal's algorithm?
A) Greedy approach
B) Dynamic programming
C) Divide and conquer
D) Backtracking
Answer: A
[cite_start]Explanation: Kruskal's algorithm uses a greedy approach by repeatedly adding the next lightest edge that does not form a cycle. [cite: 38]

Q37. The complexity of binary search algorithm is:
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n^2)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: B
[cite_start]Explanation: Binary search works on a sorted array by repeatedly dividing the search interval in half, resulting in logarithmic time complexity. [cite: 39]

Q38. A problem is said to be NP-complete if:
A) It is in NP and is as hard as any problem in NP.
B) It can be solved in polynomial time.
C) It can only be solved in exponential time.
D) It is in P.
Answer: A
[cite_start]Explanation: A problem is NP-complete if it is in the class NP (verifiable in polynomial time) and is NP-hard (at least as hard as any problem in NP). [cite: 40]

Q39. What does the 'A' in the ACID properties of a transaction stand for?

[cite_start]Explanation: Atomicity ensures that a transaction is treated as a single, indivisible unit; it either completes fully or not at all. [cite: 41]

Q74. The logical expression A + A'B is equivalent to:

Q80. The number of edges in a complete graph with 'n' vertices is:
A) n-1
B) n(n-1)
C) n(n-1)/2
D) n^2
Answer: C
[cite_start]Explanation: In a complete graph (clique), every vertex is connected to every other vertex, so the number of edges is the number of ways to choose 2 vertices from n, which is C(n, 2) = n(n-1)/2. [cite: 82]

Q81. A relation R on a set A is called reflexive if:
A) (a, a) in R for all a in A

Answer: A
[cite_start]Explanation: A relation is reflexive if every element in the set is related to itself. [cite: 83]

Q82. What is the value of P(8, 3)?
A) 24
B) 56
C) 336
D) 512
Answer: C
Explanation: The permutation formula is P(n, k) = n! / (n-k)!. So, P(8, 3) = 8! / (8-3)! = 8! / 5! [cite_start]= 8 * 7 * 6 = 336. [cite: 84]

Q99. What is the output of the following C code?

B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: B
[cite_start]Explanation: The height of a balanced binary search tree (like an AVL or Red-Black tree) with n nodes is proportional to log n, and traversing from the root to a leaf takes O(log n) time. [cite: 123]

Q122. In the context of DBMS, a view is a:
A) Base table
B) Physical table stored on disk
C) Virtual table based on the result-set of an SQL statement
D) Snapshot of a table at a specific time
Answer: C
[cite_start]Explanation: A view is not a physically stored table but a stored query that presents data from one or more underlying base tables in a structured way. [cite: 124]

Q123. The protocol that provides a connectionless datagram service at the transport layer is:
A) TCP
B) UDP
C) IP
D) FTP
Answer: B
[cite_start]Explanation: UDP (User Datagram Protocol) provides a simple, connectionless, and unreliable datagram service at the transport layer. [cite: 125]

Q124. Which data structure uses FIFO (first in first out) principle?
A) Stack
B) Queue
C) Tree
D) Graph
Answer: B
Explanation: Queue.

Q125. Which algorithm sorts by repeatedly swapping adjacent elements if they are in wrong order?
A) Selection Sort
B) Bubble Sort
C) Quick Sort
D) Insertion Sort
Answer: B
Explanation: Bubble Sort.

Q3. Which planet is known as the 'Red Planet'?
A) Venus

Q8. The deficiency of Vitamin C causes which disease?
A) Rickets
B) Scurvy
C) Beriberi
D) Night blindness
Answer: B
Explanation: Scurvy is a disease resulting from a deficiency of Vitamin C, characterized by swollen bleeding gums and the opening of previously healed wounds.

Q9. Who wrote the book 'Discovery of India'?
A) Mahatma Gandhi

C) Jawaharlal Nehru

Q10. What is the main component of Biogas?

Q11. Which Veda is primarily a collection of hymns?
A) Rigveda

D) Atharvaveda
