C) 8
D) 9
Answer: C
Explanation: The Tropic of Cancer passes through 8 Indian states: Gujarat, Rajasthan, Madhya Pradesh, Chhattisgarh, Jharkhand, West Bengal, Tripura, and Mizoram.

Q12. What is the unit of electrical resistance?
A) Volt
B) Ampere
C) Ohm
D) Watt
Answer: C
Explanation: The Ohm (Ω) is the SI derived unit of electrical resistance.

Q13. In a row of boys, If A who is 10th from the left and B who is 9th from the right interchange their positions, A becomes 15th from the left. How many boys are there in the row?
A) 23
B) 27
C) 28
D) 31
Answer: A
Explanation: After interchanging, A's new position is 15th from the left. This position was previously occupied by B, who was 9th from the right. So, Total boys = (A's new position from left + B's original position from right) - 1 = (15 + 9) - 1 = 24 - 1 = 23.

Q14. Find the missing term: 1, 4, 9, 16, 25, ?
A) 30
B) 36
C) 49
D) 64
Answer: B
Explanation: The series consists of squares of natural numbers: 1^2, 2^2, 3^2, 4^2, 5^2. The next term is 6^2 = 36.

Q15. If 'Apple' is called 'Orange', 'Orange' is called 'Peach', 'Peach' is called 'Potato', 'Potato' is called 'Banana', 'Banana' is called 'Papaya' and 'Papaya' is called 'Guava', which of the following is a vegetable?
A) Peach
B) Banana
C) Guava
D) Papaya
Answer: B
Explanation: 'Potato' is the vegetable. In the code language, 'Potato' is called 'Banana'.

Q16. Arrange the words: 1. College, 2. Child, 3. Salary, 4. School, 5. Employment
A) 1, 4, 5, 3, 2
B) 2, 4, 1, 5, 3
C) 4, 1, 3, 5, 2
D) 5, 3, 1, 4, 2
Answer: B
Explanation: The logical sequence of life stages is: Child -> School -> College -> Employment -> Salary. So, 2, 4, 1, 5, 3.

Q17. Choose the number pair which is different from others.
A) 5:25
B) 7:49
C) 9:81
D) 11:120
Answer: D
Explanation: The relationship is n : n^2. 5^2=25, 7^2=49, 9^2=81. But 11^2=121, not 120.

Q18. Pointing to a girl, Rajan said, "She is the daughter of my mother's daughter". How is the girl related to Rajan?
A) Aunt
B) Sister
C) Niece
D) Cousin
Answer: C
Explanation: "My mother's daughter" is Rajan's sister. "Daughter of my sister" is Rajan's niece.

Q19. If 'WATER' is written as 'XBUFS', how is 'BREAD' written?
A) CSFBE
B) CSDAE
C) DSDAE
D) CSEBE
Answer: A
Explanation: Each letter is shifted forward by one position (+1). B+1=C, R+1=S, E+1=F, A+1=B, D+1=E. So, CSFBE.

Q20. Find the next letters: AZ, BY, CX, ?
A) DW
B) DU
C) EV
D) DV
Answer: A
Explanation: The first letters are in alphabetical order (A, B, C, D). The second letters are in reverse alphabetical order (Z, Y, X, W). So, the next pair is DW.

Q21. Statement: Some doctors are fools. Some fools are rich. Conclusions: I. Some doctors are rich. II. Some rich are doctors.
A) Only I follows
B) Only II follows
C) Both I and II follow
D) Neither I nor II follows
Answer: D
Explanation: There is no direct link between doctors and rich people in the statements. Both conclusions are possible but not definite.

Q22. Select the related word: Thermometer : Temperature :: Barometer : ?
A) Humidity
B) Pressure
C) Wind
D) Rainfall
Answer: B
Explanation: A thermometer measures temperature. A barometer measures atmospheric pressure.

Q23. If 16 + 2 = 18, 18 + 3 = 24, 24 + 4 = 32, then 32 + 5 = ?
A) 37
B) 40
C) 42
D) 45
Answer: C
Explanation: The pattern seems to be first number + (second number * 2). 16 + (2*1) = 18? No. 16+2=18. 18+3 = 21 (not 24). Let's try 16+2=18; 18+6=24; 24+8=32; 32+10=42? Maybe the pattern is adding consecutive even numbers starting from 2? No, 2, 6, 8, 10 doesn't fit. Let's assume the operation is: a + b = a + (b * factor), where factor increases. 16 + (2*1)=18? No. Maybe a + b = a + b + (b-1)? 16+2=18; 18+3+(3-1)=23? No. Let's re-examine 16+2=18; 18+3=24; 24+4=32. The difference added is 2, 6, 8. What's the pattern? Maybe 16+2=18. 18+ (2*3) = 24. 24 + (2*4) = 32. Then 32 + (2*5) = 42.

Q24. Three of the following four are alike. Find the odd one out: Run, Walk, Swim, Think
A) Run
B) Walk
C) Swim
D) Think
Answer: D
Explanation: Run, Walk, and Swim are physical activities. Think is a mental activity.

Q25. Which number will replace the question mark? 5, 13, 29, 61, 125, ?
A) 250
B) 251
C) 253
D) 255
Answer: C
Explanation: The pattern is roughly doubling and adding a small number. 5*2+3 = 13; 13*2+3 = 29; 29*2+3 = 61; 61*2+3 = 125; 125*2+3 = 250+3 = 253.

Q26. Which of the following is NOT a data type in C?
A) int
B) float
C) string
D) char
Answer: C
Explanation: C does not have a built-in string data type; strings are handled as arrays of characters (char[]).

Q27. What is the output of the C expression `3 + 5 * 2`?
A) 16
B) 13
C) 11
D) Error
Answer: B
Explanation: Operator precedence dictates multiplication (*) is done before addition (+). So, 5 * 2 = 10, then 3 + 10 = 13.

Q28. Which keyword is used to define a constant in C?
A) constant
B) const
C) define
D) final
Answer: B
Explanation: The `const` keyword is used to declare variables whose values cannot be changed. `#define` is a preprocessor directive also used for constants.

Q29. What does the `break` statement do in a loop?
A) Skips the current iteration
B) Exits the loop immediately
C) Restarts the loop
D) Halts the program
Answer: B
Explanation: The `break` statement terminates the innermost loop or switch statement it is in.

Q30. Which data structure is typically implemented using an array where the last element added is the first one removed?
A) Queue
B) Stack
C) Linked List
D) Tree
Answer: B
Explanation: A stack follows the LIFO (Last-In, First-Out) principle.

Q31. Pre-order traversal visits nodes in which order?
A) Left, Root, Right
B) Root, Left, Right
C) Left, Right, Root
D) Root, Right, Left
Answer: B
Explanation: Pre-order traversal processes the root node first, then recursively traverses the left subtree, then the right subtree.

Q32. What is the time complexity of searching for an element in an unsorted array of size n?
A) O(1)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: In the worst case, you might have to check every element, leading to O(n) complexity (linear search).

Q33. Which algorithm design technique involves breaking a problem down into smaller, similar subproblems?
A) Greedy
B) Dynamic Programming
C) Divide and Conquer
D) Backtracking
Answer: C
Explanation: Divide and Conquer recursively breaks down a problem into two or more sub-problems of the same or related type, until these become simple enough to be solved directly.

Q34. A graph where edges have directions is called:
A) Undirected graph
B) Directed graph (Digraph)
C) Weighted graph
D) Complete graph
Answer: B
Explanation: A directed graph or digraph has edges with an associated direction.

Q35. Which sorting algorithm has an average time complexity of O(n log n) but a worst-case of O(n^2)?
A) Merge Sort
B) Heap Sort
C) Quick Sort
D) Bubble Sort
Answer: C
Explanation: Quick Sort's performance heavily depends on pivot selection; poor pivots lead to O(n^2) worst-case time.

Q36. Which data structure stores key-value pairs and allows efficient lookup, insertion, and deletion on average?
A) Array
B) Linked List
C) Hash Table (Hash Map)
D) Stack
Answer: C
Explanation: Hash tables provide average O(1) time complexity for these operations.

Q37. Which process state indicates the process is waiting for the CPU?
A) New
B) Running
C) Waiting (Blocked)
D) Ready
Answer: D
Explanation: The Ready state means the process has everything it needs to run but is waiting for its turn on the CPU.

Q38. Which memory management technique divides processes into fixed-size blocks?
A) Paging
B) Segmentation
C) Contiguous Allocation
D) Swapping
Answer: A
Explanation: Paging divides logical memory into fixed-size blocks called pages and physical memory into frames.

Q39. What is the purpose of a semaphore in operating systems?
A) Memory allocation
B) CPU scheduling
C) Process synchronization
D) File management
Answer: C
Explanation: Semaphores are used to control access to shared resources by multiple processes, preventing race conditions.

Q40. Which CPU scheduling algorithm executes processes in the order they arrive?
A) Shortest Job First (SJF)
B) Round Robin (RR)
C) First-Come, First-Served (FCFS)
D) Priority Scheduling
Answer: C
Explanation: FCFS is a simple algorithm where the process that requests the CPU first is allocated the CPU first.

Q41. What does 'thrashing' refer to in the context of virtual memory?
A) High CPU utilization
B) Excessive page swapping between memory and disk
C) Frequent disk I/O errors
D) Deadlock situation
Answer: B
Explanation: Thrashing occurs when the system spends most of its time swapping pages rather than executing instructions, usually due to insufficient physical memory.

Q42. Which layer of the OSI model is responsible for logical addressing (IP addresses)?
A) Physical Layer
B) Data Link Layer
C) Network Layer
D) Transport Layer
Answer: C
Explanation: The Network Layer handles logical addressing, routing, and path determination.

Q43. What protocol is used to resolve an IP address to a MAC address?
A) DNS
B) DHCP
C) ARP
D) ICMP
Answer: C
Explanation: Address Resolution Protocol (ARP) maps Layer 3 (IP) addresses to Layer 2 (MAC) addresses within a local network segment.

Q44. Which transport layer protocol provides connection-oriented, reliable service?
A) UDP
B) TCP
C) IP
D) ICMP
Answer: B
Explanation: Transmission Control Protocol (TCP) establishes a connection and ensures reliable, ordered data delivery.

Q45. What is the function of a router in a network?
A) Connect devices within the same LAN segment
B) Regenerate signals
C) Forward packets between different networks
D) Resolve domain names
Answer: C
Explanation: Routers operate at the Network Layer to connect different networks and make decisions about forwarding packets based on IP addresses.

Q46. Which network topology connects all devices to a central hub or switch?
A) Bus
B) Ring
C) Star
D) Mesh
Answer: C
Explanation: In a star topology, all nodes are connected individually to a central point.

Q47. What does SQL stand for?
A) Standard Query Language
B) Structured Query Language
C) Simple Query Language
D) System Query Language
Answer: B
Explanation: SQL stands for Structured Query Language, used for managing and querying relational databases.

Q48. Which SQL statement is used to retrieve data from a database?
A) INSERT
B) UPDATE
C) DELETE
D) SELECT
Answer: D
Explanation: The SELECT statement is used to query and retrieve data from one or more tables.

Q49. What is a Primary Key in a relational database?
A) A key used to link tables
B) A unique identifier for a record in a table
C) A key that can contain NULL values
D) An index for faster searching
Answer: B
Explanation: A primary key uniquely identifies each row in a table and cannot be NULL.

Q50. Which normal form ensures that there are no repeating groups or multi-valued attributes?
A) First Normal Form (1NF)
B) Second Normal Form (2NF)
C) Third Normal Form (3NF)
D) Boyce-Codd Normal Form (BCNF)
Answer: A
Explanation: 1NF requires that all attribute values are atomic (indivisible) and there are no repeating groups.

Q51. What is the purpose of the `JOIN` clause in SQL?
A) To filter records
B) To sort records
C) To combine rows from two or more tables based on a related column
D) To group records
Answer: C
Explanation: JOIN operations combine data from multiple tables based on common fields.

Q52. Which component of the CPU performs calculations?
A) Control Unit (CU)
B) Arithmetic Logic Unit (ALU)
C) Registers
D) Cache
Answer: B
Explanation: The ALU executes arithmetic (addition, subtraction) and logical (AND, OR, NOT) operations.

Q53. What is cache memory used for?
A) Long-term storage
B) Storing the operating system
C) Storing frequently accessed data for faster CPU access
D) Managing I/O devices
Answer: C
Explanation: Cache is a small, fast memory that holds copies of data from frequently used main memory locations to reduce access time.

Q54. Which type of memory is volatile (loses data when power is off)?
A) ROM
B) Hard Disk Drive (HDD)
C) Solid State Drive (SSD)
D) RAM
Answer: D
Explanation: Random Access Memory (RAM) is volatile; its contents are lost when the power is turned off.

Q55. What does 'pipelining' in a CPU achieve?
A) Increases clock speed
B) Increases instruction throughput by overlapping execution stages
C) Reduces memory usage
D) Performs floating-point calculations
Answer: B
Explanation: Pipelining allows different stages of multiple instructions to execute concurrently, increasing the number of instructions completed per unit time.

Q56. Which digital logic gate outputs 1 only if all inputs are 1?
A) OR
B) AND
C) NOT
D) XOR
Answer: B
Explanation: The AND gate outputs a high signal (1) only when all of its inputs are high (1).

Q57. What is the binary representation of the decimal number 10?
A) 1000
B) 1010
C) 1100
D) 0110
Answer: B
Explanation: 10 in decimal is (1 * 2^3) + (0 * 2^2) + (1 * 2^1) + (0 * 2^0) = 8 + 0 + 2 + 0 = 10, which corresponds to the binary representation 1010.

Q58. Which phase of the compiler checks for grammatical correctness according to the language rules?
A) Lexical Analysis
B) Syntax Analysis (Parsing)
C) Semantic Analysis
D) Code Generation
Answer: B
Explanation: Syntax Analysis checks if the sequence of tokens forms a valid structure according to the grammar of the programming language.

Q59. Which type of language is directly understood by the computer hardware?
A) High-Level Language
B) Assembly Language
C) Machine Language
D) Source Code
Answer: C
Explanation: Machine language consists of binary code (0s and 1s) that the CPU can execute directly.

Q60. What is the purpose of the 'symbol table' in a compiler?
A) To store the source code
B) To store information about identifiers (variables, functions, etc.)
C) To store the generated machine code
D) To perform code optimization
Answer: B
Explanation: The symbol table keeps track of the names used in the program and their attributes like type, scope, and memory location.

Q61. Which automata model is used to recognize regular languages?
A) Pushdown Automata (PDA)
B) Turing Machine
C) Finite Automata (FA)
D) Linear Bounded Automata (LBA)
Answer: C
Explanation: Finite Automata (both Deterministic and Non-deterministic) are the formal models for recognizing regular languages.

Q62. Which software development model involves distinct, sequential phases (Requirements, Design, Implementation, Testing, Maintenance)?
A) Agile Model
B) Spiral Model
C) Waterfall Model
D) V-Model
Answer: C
Explanation: The Waterfall model follows a linear, sequential flow where each phase must be completed before the next begins.

Q63. What is the goal of 'unit testing'?
A) To test the integration between modules
B) To test individual components or modules in isolation
C) To test the system as a whole
D) To test usability from the end-user perspective
Answer: B
Explanation: Unit testing focuses on verifying the functionality of the smallest testable parts of an application, called units.

Q64. Which quality attribute refers to how easy it is to modify software?
A) Reliability
B) Performance
C) Maintainability
D) Usability
Answer: C
Explanation: Maintainability measures the ease with which software can be modified to correct faults, improve performance, or adapt to a changed environment.

Q65. What is 'regression testing'?
A) Testing new features
B) Re-testing previously tested parts after changes to ensure no new errors were introduced
C) Testing performed by end-users
D) Testing the system under heavy load
Answer: B
Explanation: Regression testing verifies that recent code changes haven't adversely affected existing features.

Q66. Which data structure allows insertion and deletion from both ends?
A) Queue
B) Stack
C) Deque (Double-Ended Queue)
D) Heap
Answer: C
Explanation: A Deque supports adding and removing elements from either the front or the back.

Q67. What is the time complexity of building a heap (heapify) from an array of n elements?
A) O(1)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: The standard bottom-up heapify algorithm takes linear time, O(n).

Q68. Which algorithm finds the Minimum Spanning Tree (MST) of a graph?
A) Dijkstra's Algorithm
B) Bellman-Ford Algorithm
C) Kruskal's Algorithm or Prim's Algorithm
D) Floyd-Warshall Algorithm
Answer: C
Explanation: Both Kruskal's and Prim's algorithms are standard methods for finding the MST.

Q69. A hash function maps keys to:
A) Sorted indices
B) Indices in a hash table
C) Other keys
D) Fixed values
Answer: B
Explanation: A hash function computes an index into an array (the hash table) from a key.

Q70. What does 'polymorphism' mean in Object-Oriented Programming?
A) Hiding implementation details
B) The ability of an object to take on many forms or respond differently based on context
C) Inheriting properties from a parent class
D) Binding data and methods together
Answer: B
Explanation: Polymorphism allows methods to do different things based on the object it is acting upon, often through method overriding or overloading.

Q71. Which access modifier in Java provides the widest accessibility?
A) private
B) protected
C) public
D) default (package-private)
Answer: C
Explanation: `public` members are accessible from anywhere.

Q72. In Python, what does the `yield` keyword do?
A) Terminates the function
B) Pauses the function saving its state and returns a value, allowing it to resume later
C) Returns multiple values at once
D) Skips the current iteration
Answer: B
Explanation: `yield` is used in generator functions to produce a sequence of values lazily.

Q73. Which HTML tag is used to create an ordered list?
A) `<ul>`
B) `<ol>`
C) `<li>`
D) `<dl>`
Answer: B
Explanation: `<ol>` stands for ordered list, which typically displays items with numbers.

Q74. What is the purpose of CSS (Cascading Style Sheets)?
A) To define the structure of a web page
B) To add interactivity to a web page
C) To describe the presentation (styling) of a web page
D) To manage server-side logic
Answer: C
Explanation: CSS is used to control the layout, colors, fonts, and overall visual appearance of HTML elements.

Q75. Which HTTP method is typically used to submit form data?
A) GET
B) POST
C) PUT
D) DELETE
Answer: B
Explanation: POST is used to send data to a server to create or update a resource, commonly used for submitting forms.

Q76. What is the primary goal of cryptography?
A) Data compression
B) Error correction
C) Secure communication in the presence of adversaries
D) Network routing
Answer: C
Explanation: Cryptography provides techniques for confidentiality, integrity, authentication, and non-repudiation.

Q77. AES (Advanced Encryption Standard) is an example of:
A) Symmetric-key cryptography
B) Asymmetric-key cryptography
C) Hash function
D) Digital signature scheme
Answer: A
Explanation: AES uses the same key for encryption and decryption.

Q78. What does a digital signature provide?
A) Confidentiality
B) Authentication, Integrity, and Non-repudiation
C) Anonymity
D) Availability
Answer: B
Explanation: Digital signatures verify the sender's identity, ensure the message hasn't been altered, and prevent the sender from denying they sent it.

Q79. Which attack involves tricking users into revealing sensitive information?
A) Denial-of-Service (DoS)
B) Phishing
C) Man-in-the-Middle (MitM)
D) SQL Injection
Answer: B
Explanation: Phishing attacks typically use deceptive emails or websites to lure victims into providing credentials or personal data.

Q80. What is the role of a firewall?
A) To speed up network connections
B) To monitor and control incoming and outgoing network traffic based on security rules
C) To store frequently accessed web pages
D) To encrypt all network traffic
Answer: B
Explanation: Firewalls act as barriers between trusted and untrusted networks.

Q81. Which type of loop in C executes at least once?
A) for loop
B) while loop
C) do-while loop
D) infinite loop
Answer: C
Explanation: The condition in a do-while loop is checked *after* the loop body executes.

Q82. What is the purpose of an index in a database?
A) To enforce constraints
B) To speed up data retrieval operations
C) To store backup data
D) To define table relationships
Answer: B
Explanation: Indexes allow the database to find rows matching specific criteria more quickly, avoiding full table scans.

Q83. Which scheduling algorithm gives each process a fixed time slice (quantum)?
A) FCFS
B) SJF
C) Round Robin
D) Priority
Answer: C
Explanation: Round Robin cycles through processes, giving each a small time quantum on the CPU.

Q84. What is the function of the `this` keyword in Java or C#?
A) To create a new object
B) To refer to the current instance of the class
C) To call a static method
D) To terminate the program
Answer: B
Explanation: `this` refers to the current object within its own methods or constructors.

Q85. Which command in Git is used to save changes to the local repository?
A) git add
B) git commit
C) git push
D) git pull
Answer: B
Explanation: `git commit` records snapshots of the tracked files into the repository's history. `git add` stages the changes first.

Q86. What is the result of the boolean expression `(5 > 3) && (2 < 1)`?
A) true
B) false
C) Error
D) 1
Answer: B
Explanation: `(5 > 3)` is true. `(2 < 1)` is false. `true && false` evaluates to false.

Q87. Which data structure would be most efficient for checking if an item is present in a collection (on average)?
A) Unsorted Array
B) Sorted Array
C) Hash Set
D) Linked List
Answer: C
Explanation: Hash sets provide average O(1) time complexity for membership testing.

Q88. What is 'Abstraction' in OOP?
A) Binding data and code
B) Inheriting features
C) Hiding complex implementation details and showing only essential features
D) Taking many forms
Answer: C
Explanation: Abstraction simplifies complex systems by modeling classes based on relevant attributes and behaviors, hiding unnecessary details.

Q89. Which network device operates at the Data Link Layer (Layer 2)?
A) Hub
B) Router
C) Switch
D) Repeater
Answer: C
Explanation: Switches use MAC addresses to forward frames within a local network segment.

Q90. What is the main difference between TCP and UDP?
A) TCP is faster
B) UDP provides error checking
C) TCP is connection-oriented and reliable, UDP is connectionless and unreliable
D) UDP is used for web browsing
Answer: C
Explanation: TCP establishes a connection and guarantees delivery, while UDP sends datagrams without guarantees.

Q91. Which sorting algorithm involves building a max-heap or min-heap?
A) Quick Sort
B) Merge Sort
C) Heap Sort
D) Insertion Sort
Answer: C
Explanation: Heap sort uses a heap data structure to efficiently sort elements.

Q92. What is the purpose of the `finally` block in exception handling (e.g., Java, C#)?
A) To catch specific exceptions
B) To execute code regardless of whether an exception occurred or not
C) To re-throw an exception
D) To define the code that might throw an exception
Answer: B
Explanation: Code in the `finally` block is guaranteed to execute after the `try` and any `catch` blocks, used for cleanup.

Q93. Which command is used to display the current directory in Linux/Unix?
A) cd
B) ls
C) pwd
D) mkdir
Answer: C
Explanation: `pwd` stands for 'print working directory'.

Q94. Which SQL clause is used to sort the result set?
A) WHERE
B) GROUP BY
C) ORDER BY
D) HAVING
Answer: C
Explanation: `ORDER BY` sorts the rows based on specified columns.

Q95. What is the primary goal of code optimization in a compiler?
A) To make the code easier to read
B) To reduce the size or improve the execution speed of the generated code
C) To check for syntax errors
D) To generate intermediate code
Answer: B
Explanation: Optimization aims to produce more efficient machine code without changing the program's observable behavior.

Q96. What is a 'zombie' process in Unix/Linux?
A) A process running in the background
B) A process that has terminated but whose parent has not yet read its exit status
C) A process waiting for I/O
D) The initial process (init)
Answer: B
Explanation: A zombie process occupies an entry in the process table until its parent process calls `wait()`.

Q97. Which HTML tag defines the main content of an HTML document?
A) `<head>`
B) `<title>`
C) `<body>`
D) `<html>`
Answer: C
Explanation: The `<body>` tag contains all the visible content of the web page.

Q98. Which type of database model represents data as nodes and edges?
A) Relational
B) Document
C) Key-Value
D) Graph
Answer: D
Explanation: Graph databases are specifically designed to handle highly connected data using nodes, edges, and properties.

Q99. What does the 'git clone' command do?
A) Creates a new branch
B) Stages changes for commit
C) Downloads a copy of an existing repository
D) Merges branches
Answer: C
Explanation: `git clone` creates a local copy of a remote Git repository.

Q100. Which CSS property is used to change the text color of an element?
A) `background-color`
B) `font-size`
C) `color`
D) `text-align`
Answer: C
Explanation: The `color` property sets the foreground color of an element's text content.

Q101. What is the output of the following C code? #include <stdio.h> int main() { int i = 5; printf("%d", ++i); return 0; }
A) 5
B) 6
C) 4
D) Error
Answer: B
Explanation: The pre-increment operator `++i` increments `i` to 6 *before* its value is used in the `printf` function.

Q102. Which data structure is best suited for implementing a system where items must be processed in the order they arrive?
A) Stack
B) Queue
C) Heap
D) Hash Table
Answer: B
Explanation: A queue follows the FIFO (First-In, First-Out) principle, matching the requirement.

Q103. Which process synchronization mechanism involves busy-waiting?
A) Semaphore (using blocking wait)
B) Mutex (using blocking wait)
C) Spinlock
D) Monitor
Answer: C
Explanation: A spinlock causes a thread trying to acquire it to simply wait in a loop ('spin') while checking if the lock is available.

Q104. What is the main purpose of the IP (Internet Protocol)?
A) To guarantee reliable data delivery
B) To provide logical addressing and routing of packets
C) To manage sessions between applications
D) To resolve domain names
Answer: B
Explanation: IP is responsible for addressing hosts and routing datagrams from a source host to a destination host across one or more IP networks.

Q105. Which SQL constraint ensures that a column cannot have NULL values?
A) UNIQUE
B) PRIMARY KEY
C) NOT NULL
D) CHECK
Answer: C
Explanation: The `NOT NULL` constraint prevents NULL values from being inserted into a column. (PRIMARY KEY also implies NOT NULL).

Q106. In Big-O notation, which complexity class grows fastest?
A) O(log n)
B) O(n)
C) O(n log n)
D) O(n^2)
Answer: D
Explanation: O(n^2) (quadratic) grows faster than logarithmic, linear, or linearithmic time for large n.

Q107. What does the `finally` clause in Python's try-except block do?
A) Catches all exceptions
B) Executes only if an exception occurs
C) Executes always, regardless of whether an exception occurred
D) Skips execution if an exception occurred
Answer: C
Explanation: The `finally` block executes after the `try` and `except` blocks, ensuring cleanup code runs.

Q108. Which HTML element is used to display an image?
A) `<image>`
B) `<pic>`
C) `<img>`
D) `<src>`
Answer: C
Explanation: The `<img>` tag is used, typically with the `src` attribute to specify the image URL.

Q109. What is the role of JavaScript in web development?
A) Styling web pages
B) Defining page structure
C) Adding interactivity and dynamic behavior to web pages
D) Managing databases
Answer: C
Explanation: JavaScript is a client-side scripting language used to make web pages interactive.

Q110. Which HTTP status code indicates success?
A) 200 OK
B) 301 Moved Permanently
C) 404 Not Found
D) 500 Internal Server Error
Answer: A
Explanation: 2xx status codes indicate success. 200 OK is the standard response for successful HTTP requests.

Q111. What is the difference between `==` and `equals()` in Java for objects?
A) No difference
B) `==` compares object references, `equals()` typically compares object content (can be overridden)
C) `equals()` compares references, `==` compares content
D) `==` is for primitives, `equals()` is for objects
Answer: B
Explanation: `==` checks if two references point to the same object in memory, while `equals()` is intended to check for logical equality based on content.

Q112. Which SQL keyword is used to filter results based on a specified condition?
A) ORDER BY
B) GROUP BY
C) WHERE
D) HAVING
Answer: C
Explanation: The `WHERE` clause filters rows *before* any grouping occurs.

Q113. What is the default port for the SSH (Secure Shell) protocol?
A) 21
B) 22
C) 23
D) 80
Answer: B
Explanation: SSH typically runs on TCP port 22.

Q114. Which algorithm is commonly used for finding the shortest path in an unweighted graph?
A) Dijkstra's Algorithm
B) Breadth-First Search (BFS)
C) Depth-First Search (DFS)
D) Bellman-Ford Algorithm
Answer: B
Explanation: BFS explores the graph layer by layer, guaranteeing the shortest path in terms of the number of edges.

Q115. What is 'Encapsulation' in OOP?
A) Inheriting properties
B) Hiding implementation details
C) Binding data (attributes) and methods (functions) that operate on the data into a single unit (object)
D) Allowing an object to take many forms
Answer: C
Explanation: Encapsulation bundles data and methods together and often restricts direct access to some components (information hiding).

Q116. Which type of memory requires refreshing?
A) SRAM (Static RAM)
B) DRAM (Dynamic RAM)
C) ROM (Read-Only Memory)
D) Flash Memory
Answer: B
Explanation: DRAM stores bits in capacitors that leak charge and thus need to be periodically refreshed to retain data.

Q117. What is the purpose of the `alt` attribute in an HTML `<img>` tag?
A) To specify the image URL
B) To provide alternative text for the image (for accessibility and if the image fails to load)
C) To set the image width
D) To link the image to another page
Answer: B
Explanation: The `alt` attribute provides a textual description of the image.

Q118. Which Linux command is used to change file permissions?
A) chown
B) chmod
C) chgrp
D) ls
Answer: B
Explanation: `chmod` (change mode) modifies the read, write, and execute permissions for files and directories.

Q119. What is the function of an API (Application Programming Interface)?
A) To provide a graphical user interface
B) To define how software components should interact with each other
C) To store large amounts of data
D) To compile source code
Answer: B
Explanation: An API specifies a set of rules, protocols, and tools for building software applications, defining interactions.

Q120. Which principle suggests that software entities (classes, modules, functions) should be open for extension but closed for modification?
A) Single Responsibility Principle (SRP)
B) Open/Closed Principle (OCP)
C) Liskov Substitution Principle (LSP)
D) Dependency Inversion Principle (DIP)
Answer: B
Explanation: The OCP promotes extending behavior without changing existing code, reducing the risk of introducing bugs.

Q121. What is the role of a DNS server?
A) To assign IP addresses
B) To translate domain names into IP addresses
C) To route network traffic
D) To store website files
Answer: B
Explanation: The Domain Name System (DNS) acts like a phonebook for the internet, resolving human-readable names to numerical IP addresses.

Q122. Which algorithm design paradigm builds up a solution by choosing the locally optimal option at each step?
A) Divide and Conquer
B) Dynamic Programming
C) Greedy Algorithm
D) Backtracking
Answer: C
Explanation: Greedy algorithms make the choice that seems best at the moment, hoping it leads to a global optimum.

Q123. What is the binary equivalent of the decimal number 5?
A) 100
B) 101
C) 110
D) 011
Answer: B
Explanation: 5 = 4 + 1 = (1 * 2^2) + (0 * 2^1) + (1 * 2^0), which is 101 in binary.

Q124. In CSS, what does the 'padding' property control?
A) The space between the element's border and its content
B) The space outside the element's border
C) The thickness of the element's border
D) The font size of the element's content
Answer: A
Explanation: Padding is the inner space between the content and the border. Margin is the outer space.

Q125. Which software testing level focuses on testing the interactions between integrated modules?
A) Unit Testing
B) Integration Testing
C) System Testing
D) Acceptance Testing
Answer: B
Explanation: Integration testing verifies that different modules or services work together as expected.

SET 9 (BEL)

Q1. Which data structure is typically used to implement a dictionary or associative array?
A) Stack
B) Queue
C) Hash Table
D) Linked List
Answer: C
Explanation: Hash tables provide average O(1) lookup, insertion, and deletion, making them ideal for dictionaries.

Q2. What is the worst-case time complexity for searching an element in a general Binary Search Tree (BST)?
A) O(1)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: In the worst case (a skewed tree resembling a linked list), the search degenerates to O(n).

Q3. Which algorithm paradigm does Merge Sort belong to?
A) Greedy
B) Dynamic Programming
C) Divide and Conquer
D) Backtracking
Answer: C
Explanation: Merge Sort recursively divides the array into halves, sorts them, and merges the results.

Q4. A complete binary tree with 'n' nodes has a height of approximately:
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(1)
D) O(n^2)
Answer: B
Explanation: A complete (or balanced) binary tree has a logarithmic height with respect to the number of nodes.

Q5. Which data structure allows efficient insertion and deletion at any arbitrary position, but slow random access?
A) Array
B) Doubly Linked List
C) Hash Table
D) Stack
Answer: B
Explanation: Linked lists allow O(1) insertion/deletion if the node's position (or adjacent node) is known, but accessing the k-th element takes O(k) time.

Q6. What is the time complexity of the Depth First Search (DFS) algorithm on a graph represented by an adjacency list?
A) O(V^2)
B) O(E log V)
C) O(V + E)
D) O(V * E)
Answer: C
Explanation: DFS visits each vertex and edge once in an adjacency list representation, resulting in O(V + E) complexity.

Q7. Which sorting algorithm selects the smallest (or largest) element from the unsorted portion and swaps it into its correct position?
A) Bubble Sort
B) Insertion Sort
C) Selection Sort
D) Merge Sort
Answer: C
Explanation: Selection sort repeatedly selects the minimum element and places it at the beginning of the unsorted part.

Q8. What does it mean for a hash function to be "uniform"?
A) It always produces the same output.
B) It maps keys to indices as evenly as possible.
C) It works only for integers.
D) It is easily reversible.
Answer: B
Explanation: A uniform hash function minimizes collisions by distributing keys evenly across the hash table slots.

Q9. Which data structure is typically used to manage function calls and local variables in a program?
A) Queue
B) Heap
C) Stack
D) Hash Table
Answer: C
Explanation: The call stack (or execution stack) stores activation records for active function calls.

Q10. What is the time complexity to check if a queue implemented with a circular array is full? (Assuming size, front, rear are known)
A) O(1)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: A
Explanation: Checking the full condition, like `(rear + 1) % size == front`, takes constant time.

Q11. Dijkstra's algorithm may fail if the graph contains:
A) Cycles
B) Negative edge weights
C) Multiple sources
D) Disconnected components
Answer: B
Explanation: Dijkstra's greedy approach does not work correctly with negative edge weights; Bellman-Ford should be used instead.

Q12. What property must a binary tree satisfy to be a Binary Search Tree (BST)?
A) All nodes must have exactly two children.
B) The value of every node must be greater than all values in its left subtree and less than all values in its right subtree.
C) It must be a complete binary tree.
D) The root node must contain the smallest value.
Answer: B
Explanation: This is the fundamental ordering property that defines a BST and allows efficient searching.

Q13. Which algorithm is used to find all connected components in an undirected graph?
A) Dijkstra's Algorithm
B) Prim's Algorithm
C) BFS or DFS
D) Floyd-Warshall Algorithm
Answer: C
Explanation: Both Breadth-First Search and Depth-First Search can be adapted to find all vertices reachable from a starting vertex, thus identifying connected components.

Q14. What is the space complexity of inserting an element into a stack implemented using an array (assuming capacity is sufficient)?
A) O(n)
B) O(log n)
C) O(1)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: Pushing onto an array-based stack (if not full) only involves updating the top pointer and placing the element, requiring constant extra space.

Q15. Which of the following is an example of a greedy algorithm?
A) Merge Sort
B) Kruskal's algorithm for MST
C) Floyd-Warshall algorithm
D) Breadth-First Search
Answer: B
Explanation: Kruskal's algorithm greedily selects the next cheapest edge that doesn't form a cycle.

Q16. What is the primary purpose of memory management in an OS?
A) To execute user commands
B) To manage the allocation and deallocation of memory space to processes
C) To handle network communication
D) To manage file storage
Answer: B
Explanation: The OS memory manager tracks memory usage, allocates space to processes, and reclaims it when processes terminate.

Q17. Which condition is necessary but not sufficient for deadlock?
A) Mutual Exclusion
B) Hold and Wait
C) No Preemption
D) Circular Wait
Answer: D
Explanation: Circular wait implies the other three conditions might be present, but the presence of the first three doesn't guarantee a circular wait (and thus deadlock). However, all four *together* are necessary and sufficient. Among the options, circular wait is often seen as the culmination.

Q18. Which scheduling algorithm provides the lowest average response time for interactive systems?
A) FCFS
B) SJF (Non-preemptive)
C) Round Robin
D) Priority (Non-preemptive)
Answer: C
Explanation: Round Robin with a reasonable time quantum gives all processes frequent, short bursts of CPU time, improving responsiveness.

Q19. What is the function of the `fork()` system call in UNIX/Linux?
A) To execute a new program
B) To terminate the current process
C) To create a new child process, which is a copy of the parent
D) To wait for a child process to terminate
Answer: C
Explanation: `fork()` creates a near-identical copy of the calling process.

Q20. Virtual memory allows a process to:
A) Run faster than using physical memory alone
B) Use more memory than is physically available
C) Directly access hardware devices
D) Share memory with the kernel exclusively
Answer: B
Explanation: Virtual memory uses disk space as an extension of RAM, allowing processes larger than physical memory to run.

Q21. Which page replacement algorithm suffers from Belady's Anomaly?
A) LRU (Least Recently Used)
B) Optimal
C) FIFO (First-In, First-Out)
D) Clock
Answer: C
Explanation: Belady's Anomaly is the phenomenon where increasing the number of page frames results in an increase in the number of page faults for certain access patterns, which can occur with FIFO.

Q22. What is the role of the MMU (Memory Management Unit)?
A) Performing arithmetic calculations
B) Translating virtual addresses to physical addresses
C) Scheduling processes
D) Managing network packets
Answer: B
Explanation: The MMU hardware handles the translation between the logical addresses used by processes and the physical addresses in RAM.

Q23. Which synchronization primitive allows multiple processes/threads to wait until all of them reach a certain point?
A) Mutex
B) Semaphore
C) Monitor
D) Barrier
Answer: D
Explanation: A barrier synchronizes multiple threads; threads arriving at the barrier wait until all participating threads have arrived.

Q24. What type of operating system is designed to handle tasks with strict timing requirements?
A) Batch OS
B) Time-Sharing OS
C) Real-Time OS (RTOS)
D) Distributed OS
Answer: C
Explanation: RTOS guarantees that critical tasks complete within specific deadlines.

Q25. Which file system component stores metadata about files (like permissions, owner, size, location)?
A) Superblock
B) Boot block
C) Inode (in Unix-like systems) or MFT entry (in NTFS)
D) Data blocks
Answer: C
Explanation: Inodes (Index Nodes) contain essential metadata for each file or directory.

Q26. Which layer of the TCP/IP model corresponds to the OSI model's Network Layer?
A) Application Layer
B) Transport Layer
C) Internet Layer
D) Network Access Layer
Answer: C
Explanation: The Internet Layer in TCP/IP (handling IP addressing and routing) maps closely to the OSI Network Layer.

Q27. What is the maximum number of hosts possible in a Class C network?
A) 256
B) 254
C) 65534
D) 126
Answer: B
Explanation: A Class C network uses 24 bits for the network ID, leaving 8 bits for the host ID. This allows 2^8 = 256 addresses, but the all-zeros (network) and all-ones (broadcast) addresses are reserved, leaving 254 usable host addresses.

Q28. Which protocol provides connectionless, unreliable datagram service?
A) TCP
B) UDP
C) IP
D) HTTP
Answer: B
Explanation: User Datagram Protocol (UDP) offers minimal overhead but no guarantees of delivery, order, or error correction beyond basic checksums.

Q29. What is the purpose of the subnet mask?
A) To identify the physical address
B) To distinguish the network portion from the host portion of an IP address
C) To encrypt data packets
D) To assign port numbers
Answer: B
Explanation: The subnet mask allows devices and routers to determine if a destination IP address is on the local network or needs to be routed elsewhere.

Q30. Which network device operates primarily at the Physical Layer (Layer 1)?
A) Router
B) Switch
C) Hub
D) Firewall
Answer: C
Explanation: A hub simply repeats electrical signals received on one port to all other ports without inspecting addresses; it's a basic physical layer device.

Q31. What protocol is used by the `ping` command?
A) TCP
B) UDP
C) ICMP
D) ARP
Answer: C
Explanation: `ping` uses ICMP Echo Request and Echo Reply messages to test connectivity.

Q32. Which type of address is used by switches to forward frames?
A) IP Address
B) Port Number
C) MAC Address
D) Domain Name
Answer: C
Explanation: Switches operate at Layer 2 and use MAC (Media Access Control) addresses to direct traffic within a LAN segment.

Q33. Which organization is primarily responsible for assigning domain names and IP addresses globally?
A) IEEE
B) IETF
C) ICANN
D) ISO
Answer: C
Explanation: The Internet Corporation for Assigned Names and Numbers (ICANN) coordinates the allocation and assignment of top-level domain names and IP addresses.

Q34. What does NAT stand for?
A) Network Address Translation
B) Network Access Time
C) Node Addressing Table
D) Network Administration Tool
Answer: A
Explanation: NAT allows multiple devices on a private network to share a single public IP address.

Q35. Which routing protocol type calculates the best path based on the number of hops?
A) Link-State (e.g., OSPF)
B) Distance-Vector (e.g., RIP)
C) Path-Vector (e.g., BGP)
D) Hybrid
Answer: B
Explanation: Distance-vector protocols like RIP use hop count as their primary metric.

Q36. Which normal form is violated if a non-prime attribute is functionally dependent on another non-prime attribute?
A) 1NF
B) 2NF
C) 3NF
D) BCNF
Answer: C
Explanation: This describes a transitive dependency, which is eliminated in Third Normal Form (3NF).

Q37. Which SQL statement is used to add new data into a table?
A) `SELECT`
B) `UPDATE`
C) `INSERT INTO`
D) `CREATE TABLE`
Answer: C
Explanation: `INSERT INTO` is used to add one or more rows to a table.

Q38. What does the ACID property 'Durability' guarantee?
A) Transactions are indivisible.
B) Database constraints are maintained.
C) Concurrent transactions do not interfere improperly.
D) Once a transaction is committed, its effects persist even if the system crashes.
Answer: D
Explanation: Durability ensures that committed changes are permanently stored (usually in non-volatile memory like disk).

Q39. Which relational algebra operation returns columns of a relation?
A) Selection (σ)
B) Projection (π)
C) Union (∪)
D) Cartesian Product (×)
Answer: B
Explanation: Projection selects specified attributes (columns) from a relation, discarding duplicates.

Q40. What is the purpose of an index scan in database query processing?
A) To read the entire table sequentially
B) To use an index structure to find rows matching a condition more quickly
C) To sort the data before retrieval
D) To join multiple tables
Answer: B
Explanation: An index scan (or index seek) uses the index to directly locate or narrow down the search for relevant data blocks/rows.

Q41. Which join type returns only the rows where the join condition is met in both tables?
A) LEFT JOIN
B) RIGHT JOIN
C) FULL OUTER JOIN
D) INNER JOIN
Answer: D
Explanation: INNER JOIN selects rows that have matching values in both tables involved in the join.

Q42. What is a 'candidate key'?
A) A key chosen as the primary identifier for a table.
B) A key used to link to another table.
C) Any attribute or set of attributes that can uniquely identify a tuple in a relation.
D) A key containing NULL values.
Answer: C
Explanation: A relation may have multiple candidate keys, one of which is designated as the primary key.

Q43. Which SQL clause is used to filter results *after* grouping has occurred?
A) `WHERE`
B) `GROUP BY`
C) `HAVING`
D) `ORDER BY`
Answer: C
Explanation: `HAVING` filters groups based on aggregate conditions, whereas `WHERE` filters rows before grouping.

Q44. What type of database relationship exists between 'Students' and 'Courses' when a student can enroll in many courses, and a course can have many students?
A) One-to-One (1:1)
B) One-to-Many (1:N)
C) Many-to-One (N:1)
D) Many-to-Many (N:M)
Answer: D
Explanation: This scenario requires a Many-to-Many relationship, often implemented using an intermediate junction table.

Q45. What is the main goal of database normalization?
A) To maximize data redundancy
B) To minimize data redundancy and improve data integrity
C) To speed up all queries
D) To simplify database backups
Answer: B
Explanation: Normalization organizes data to reduce duplication and avoid anomalies during data insertion, update, or deletion.

Q46. Which CPU component fetches instructions from memory?
A) ALU
B) Registers
C) Control Unit
D) Cache
Answer: C
Explanation: The Control Unit manages the instruction fetch-decode-execute cycle, including fetching the next instruction based on the Program Counter.

Q47. What is 'Instruction Level Parallelism' (ILP)?
A) Running multiple processes simultaneously
B) Executing multiple instructions from a single program concurrently within the CPU
C) Using multiple cores to run different programs
D) Increasing the CPU clock speed
Answer: B
Explanation: Techniques like pipelining and superscalar execution exploit ILP to improve performance.

Q48. Which memory type stores the computer's startup instructions (BIOS/UEFI)?
A) RAM
B) Cache
C) ROM (or Flash memory used as ROM)
D) Hard Disk
Answer: C
Explanation: Read-Only Memory (or its modern equivalent like Flash) holds the firmware needed to boot the system.

Q49. What is the purpose of a bus in a computer system?
A) To perform calculations
B) To store data permanently
C) To provide communication pathways between components (CPU, memory, I/O)
D) To manage power distribution
Answer: C
Explanation: Buses (address bus, data bus, control bus) are shared communication lines for transferring data and control signals.

Q50. Which number system is directly understood by digital circuits?
A) Decimal
B) Hexadecimal
C) Octal
D) Binary
Answer: D
Explanation: Digital logic operates using two states (high/low voltage), naturally represented by binary digits (0 and 1).

Q51. What is the function of a flip-flop circuit?
A) To perform arithmetic operations
B) To store a single bit of information
C) To select between multiple inputs
D) To convert analog signals to digital
Answer: B
Explanation: Flip-flops are fundamental sequential logic circuits used as memory elements in registers and counters.

Q52. Convert the hexadecimal number 'A' to binary.
A) 1000
B) 1010
C) 1100
D) 1001
Answer: B
Explanation: Hexadecimal A represents decimal 10, which is 1010 in binary (8 + 2).

Q53. Which logic gate is known as the universal gate because others can be built from it?
A) AND
B) OR
C) NOT
D) NAND (or NOR)
Answer: D
Explanation: Both NAND gates and NOR gates are functionally complete; any other logic function can be implemented using only NANDs or only NORs.

Q54. What does the term 'endianness' refer to?
A) The clock speed of the CPU
B) The order in which bytes are stored in memory for multi-byte data types
C) The type of cache memory used
D) The instruction set architecture
Answer: B
Explanation: It specifies whether the least significant byte (Little-endian) or the most significant byte (Big-endian) is stored at the lowest memory address.

Q55. Which type of addressing mode uses the value in a register as the memory address of the operand?
A) Immediate
B) Direct
C) Register Indirect
D) Indexed
Answer: C
Explanation: In register indirect addressing, the instruction specifies a register that contains the *address* of the data, not the data itself.

Q56. Which automaton has a stack in addition to finite control?
A) Finite Automaton (FA)
B) Pushdown Automaton (PDA)
C) Turing Machine
D) Linear Bounded Automaton (LBA)
Answer: B
Explanation: The stack gives PDAs more memory capabilities than FAs, allowing them to recognize context-free languages.

Q57. The process of checking if a string belongs to the language generated by a grammar is called:
A) Lexing
B) Parsing (Syntax Analysis)
C) Semantic Analysis
D) Code Generation
Answer: B
Explanation: Parsing determines if a string conforms to the grammatical structure defined by a formal grammar, often building a parse tree.

Q58. Which type of grammar has unrestricted production rules (α -> β)?
A) Type 3 (Regular)
B) Type 2 (Context-Free)
C) Type 1 (Context-Sensitive)
D) Type 0 (Recursively Enumerable/Unrestricted)
Answer: D
Explanation: Type 0 grammars have no restrictions on their production rules and correspond to Turing machines.

Q59. What is the purpose of the 'Follow set' in compiler design (specifically for LL parsing)?
A) To determine the first possible terminals derivable from a non-terminal
B) To determine the terminals that can appear immediately *after* a non-terminal in a valid derivation
C) To store variable names
D) To optimize loops
Answer: B
Explanation: Follow sets are used, along with First sets, to construct LL(1) parsing tables and resolve parsing conflicts.

Q60. Which phase of the compiler deals with type checking?
A) Lexical Analysis
B) Syntax Analysis
C) Semantic Analysis
D) Intermediate Code Generation
Answer: C
Explanation: Semantic analysis checks for meaning-related errors, including type mismatches between operands and operators.

Q61. What is 'Agile' methodology in software development?
A) A strict, sequential process
B) A methodology emphasizing iterative development, collaboration, and rapid response to change
C) A model focused solely on documentation
D) A risk-driven process model
Answer: B
Explanation: Agile principles prioritize working software, customer collaboration, and adapting to changing requirements over rigid planning and processes.

Q62. What does 'Scrum' primarily define?
A) A specific programming language
B) A framework for managing Agile projects, involving roles, events, and artifacts
C) A type of software testing
D) A database model
Answer: B
Explanation: Scrum provides a structure (sprints, daily stand-ups, backlog, etc.) for implementing Agile development.

Q63. Which testing level verifies if the system meets the user's requirements?
A) Unit Testing
B) Integration Testing
C) System Testing
D) Acceptance Testing
Answer: D
Explanation: Acceptance testing is typically performed by the client or end-users to determine if the system satisfies their needs and is acceptable for deployment.

Q64. What is 'Refactoring'?
A) Adding new features to the software
B) Fixing bugs
C) Restructuring existing computer code without changing its external behavior
D) Writing documentation
Answer: C
Explanation: Refactoring improves code quality (readability, maintainability) without altering its functionality.

Q65. Which diagram type in UML (Unified Modeling Language) is used to model the interactions between objects over time?
A) Class Diagram
B) Use Case Diagram
C) Sequence Diagram
D) State Machine Diagram
Answer: C
Explanation: Sequence diagrams depict object interactions arranged in time sequence, showing the messages passed between objects.

Q66. What is the output of `printf("%d", 10 / 3);` in C?
A) 3.3333
B) 3.0
C) 3
D) Error
Answer: C
Explanation: In C, division between two integers results in an integer (truncation occurs). 10 / 3 = 3.

Q67. Which collection class in Java represents a LIFO stack?
A) `ArrayList`
B) `LinkedList`
C) `Stack` (legacy) or using `Deque` interface (e.g., `ArrayDeque`)
D) `HashSet`
Answer: C
Explanation: The `Stack` class provides standard stack operations. Modern practice often favors using a `Deque` implementation like `ArrayDeque`.

Q68. In Python, what does the expression `[i*i for i in range(3)]` evaluate to?
A) `[0, 1, 2]`
B) `[1, 4, 9]`
C) `[0, 1, 4]`
D) Error
Answer: C
Explanation: This is a list comprehension. `range(3)` produces 0, 1, 2. The expression `i*i` squares each number: 0*0=0, 1*1=1, 2*2=4. Result: `[0, 1, 4]`.

Q69. Which keyword is used to handle exceptions in Java/C#/Python?
A) `try`, `catch` (Java/C#) / `except` (Python), `finally`
B) `if`, `else`
C) `for`, `while`
D) `throw`, `throws`
Answer: A
Explanation: The `try` block contains code that might raise an exception, `catch`/`except` blocks handle specific exceptions, and `finally` executes cleanup code.

Q70. What is the purpose of the `static` keyword in Java (when applied to a method)?
A) The method can only be called on instances of the class.
B) The method belongs to the class itself, not to any specific instance, and can be called using the class name.
C) The method cannot be overridden.
D) The method is automatically executed.
Answer: B
Explanation: Static methods are associated with the class and don't operate on instance-specific data (unless passed explicitly).

Q71. Which HTML tag defines emphasized text, typically displayed in italics?
A) `<b>`
B) `<i>`
C) `<em>`
D) `<strong>`
Answer: C
Explanation: `<em>` indicates semantic emphasis. While `<i>` also displays italics, `<em>` is preferred for semantic meaning. `<strong>` indicates importance (bold). `<b>` is just bold.

Q72. What is the role of HTTP cookies?
A) To store large files on the client-side
B) To allow servers to store small pieces of state information on the user's browser
C) To execute server-side code
D) To encrypt web traffic
Answer: B
Explanation: Cookies are used to maintain session information, track users, and store preferences between HTTP requests.

Q73. Which JavaScript function is used to print output to the browser's console?
A) `alert()`
B) `document.write()`
C) `console.log()`
D) `prompt()`
Answer: C
Explanation: `console.log()` is the standard way to output debugging information or other messages to the developer console.

Q74. What does JSON stand for?
A) Java Standard Object Notation
B) JavaScript Object Notation
C) Java Syntax Object Notation
D) JavaScript Standard Object Notation
Answer: B
Explanation: JSON is a lightweight data-interchange format inspired by JavaScript object literal syntax.

Q75. Which CSS property is used to control the layout of items in one dimension (row or column)?
A) Grid Layout
B) Flexbox (`display: flex`)
C) Float
D) Position
Answer: B
Explanation: Flexbox is designed for one-dimensional layouts, distributing space along a single axis. Grid is for two-dimensional layouts.

Q76. Which type of ML algorithm predicts a continuous value?
A) Classification
B) Regression
C) Clustering
D) Dimensionality Reduction
Answer: B
Explanation: Regression algorithms (like Linear Regression) predict numerical outcomes.

Q77. What is 'feature engineering' in machine learning?
A) Selecting the best algorithm
B) Training the model
C) Creating new input features from existing data or transforming features to improve model performance
D) Evaluating the model
Answer: C
Explanation: Feature engineering involves using domain knowledge to create features that make ML algorithms work better.

Q78. K-Means algorithm is sensitive to:
A) Outliers and initial centroid placement
B) The number of features
C) Labeled data only
D) The learning rate
Answer: A
Explanation: Outliers can significantly skew centroid positions, and different initializations can lead to different final clusters.

Q79. What is the purpose of a 'validation set' in ML model development?
A) To train the model
B) To tune hyperparameters and make decisions about the model architecture
C) To provide a final, unbiased evaluation of the model's performance
D) To preprocess the data
Answer: B
Explanation: The validation set helps select the best model configuration without overfitting to the test set. The test set is used for the final evaluation.

Q80. Which metric is calculated as TP / (TP + FP)?
A) Recall (Sensitivity)
B) Precision
C) Accuracy
D) Specificity
Answer: B
Explanation: Precision measures the proportion of predicted positive instances that were actually positive.

Q81. What is the function of an Activation Function in a neural network neuron?
A) To normalize the input data
B) To calculate the weighted sum of inputs
C) To introduce non-linearity into the model's output
D) To initialize the weights
Answer: C
Explanation: Non-linear activation functions allow neural networks to learn complex patterns that linear models cannot capture.

Q82. Which big data framework introduced the MapReduce programming model?
A) Apache Spark
B) Apache Flink
C) Apache Hadoop
D) Apache Kafka
Answer: C
Explanation: Hadoop was the pioneering framework that implemented Google's MapReduce paradigm for distributed processing.

Q83. What does 'gradient descent' aim to do?
A) Maximize a cost function
B) Minimize a cost function by iteratively moving in the direction of the steepest descent
C) Classify data points
D) Cluster data points
Answer: B
Explanation: It's an optimization algorithm used to find the minimum of a function, often the loss function in ML.

Q84. Which type of ML model is well-suited for sequence prediction tasks (like time series or text)?
A) K-Means
B) Linear Regression
C) Recurrent Neural Network (RNN) or LSTM
D) Support Vector Machine (SVM)
Answer: C
Explanation: RNNs and their variants like LSTMs are designed to handle sequential data by maintaining an internal state or memory.

Q85. What is 'One-Hot Encoding'?
A) A dimensionality reduction technique
B) A method for handling missing data
C) A technique to convert categorical variables into a numerical format suitable for ML algorithms
D) A type of clustering algorithm
Answer: C
Explanation: It creates binary columns for each category, with a 1 indicating the presence of that category for a given instance and 0 otherwise.

Q86. What is the key difference between a Virus and a Worm?
A) Viruses target files, Worms target networks.
B) Viruses require human action (e.g., opening a file) to spread, Worms can self-replicate across networks.
C) Worms are less harmful than Viruses.
D) Viruses encrypt data, Worms steal data.
Answer: B
Explanation: Worms are standalone malware that actively transmit themselves, while viruses typically attach to other files and need user interaction to propagate.

Q87. What does HTTPS provide that HTTP does not?
A) Faster loading speed
B) Caching capabilities
C) Encryption of data in transit (using TLS/SSL)
D) Domain name resolution
Answer: C
Explanation: HTTPS secures the communication channel between the client and server, providing confidentiality and integrity.

Q88. What is the purpose of a VPN (Virtual Private Network)?
A) To increase internet speed
B) To create a secure, encrypted connection over a public network (like the internet)
C) To block specific websites
D) To assign static IP addresses
Answer: B
Explanation: VPNs tunnel network traffic securely, often used for privacy or accessing restricted networks remotely.

Q89. Which security principle involves granting only the necessary permissions required to perform a task?
A) Defense in Depth
B) Principle of Least Privilege
C) Security through Obscurity
D) Open Design
Answer: B
Explanation: Limiting permissions minimizes the potential damage if an account or process is compromised.

Q90. What is a 'Man-in-the-Middle' (MitM) attack?
A) Overwhelming a server with traffic
B) Tricking a user into revealing credentials
C) Secretly intercepting and possibly altering communications between two parties
D) Installing malware via email attachment
Answer: C
Explanation: The attacker positions themselves between the victim and the legitimate server/party they are communicating with.

Q91. What is the purpose of `public static void main(String[] args)` in Java?
A) It's the entry point for executing a Java application.
B) It defines a class constructor.
C) It declares instance variables.
D) It handles exceptions.
Answer: A
Explanation: The Java Virtual Machine (JVM) looks for this specific method signature to start program execution.

Q92. In Python, which data structure stores items in an unordered manner and does not allow duplicate elements?
A) List
B) Tuple
C) Dictionary
D) Set
Answer: D
Explanation: Sets store unique elements in an unordered collection.

Q93. What is the complexity of finding the k-th smallest element in an unsorted array using a comparison-based algorithm (worst-case optimal)?
A) O(1)
B) O(log n)
C) O(n)
D) O(n log n)
Answer: C
Explanation: Algorithms like Quickselect provide an average time of O(n), and there are deterministic algorithms (like Median of Medians) that achieve O(n) in the worst case.

Q94. Which type of database replication involves multiple nodes being able to accept writes?
A) Master-Slave (Leader-Follower)
B) Multi-Master
C) Snapshot Replication
D) Transactional Replication
Answer: B
Explanation: Multi-master replication allows writes on any node, requiring mechanisms to resolve potential conflicts.

Q95. What is the role of the `ClassLoader` in Java?
A) To compile Java code
B) To dynamically load Java classes into the JVM at runtime
C) To manage memory allocation
D) To handle network sockets
Answer: B
Explanation: ClassLoaders are responsible for finding and loading class files when they are needed.

Q96. Which is a characteristic of microservices architecture?
A) Single large codebase
B) Services are independently deployable and scalable
C) Shared database among all services
D) Tight coupling between services
Answer: B
Explanation: Microservices break down an application into small, autonomous services that communicate over a network.

Q97. What does the 'git merge' command do?
A) Creates a new repository
B) Deletes a branch
C) Combines changes from different branches into one
D) Shows the commit history
Answer: C
Explanation: `git merge` integrates changes from a specified branch into the current branch.

Q98. Which layer in the OSI model is responsible for process-to-process communication?
A) Network Layer
B) Data Link Layer
C) Session Layer
D) Transport Layer
Answer: D
Explanation: The Transport Layer (using protocols like TCP and UDP with port numbers) provides communication services directly to application processes.

Q99. What is the purpose of garbage collection in languages like Java and Python?
A) To compile code
B) To automatically reclaim memory occupied by objects that are no longer referenced
C) To handle user input
D) To manage file permissions
Answer: B
Explanation: Automatic garbage collection frees developers from manual memory deallocation, reducing memory leaks.

Q100. Which type of database constraint enforces that values in a column must match values in another table's primary key column?
A) NOT NULL
B) UNIQUE
C) PRIMARY KEY
D) FOREIGN KEY
Answer: D
Explanation: Foreign keys establish and enforce links between tables, maintaining referential integrity.

Q101. Convert binary 11001 to decimal.
A) 20
B) 25
C) 27
D) 31
Answer: B
Explanation: (1*16) + (1*8) + (0*4) + (0*2) + (1*1) = 16 + 8 + 1 = 25.

Q102. What is the output of the logical OR operation: 1 OR 0?
A) 0
B) 1
C) Undefined
D) -1
Answer: B
Explanation: The OR operation results in 1 (true) if at least one of the inputs is 1 (true).

Q103. Which scheduling algorithm is generally best for batch processing systems?
A) Round Robin
B) FCFS or SJF (Non-preemptive)
C) Real-time scheduling
D) Interactive priority scheduling
Answer: B
Explanation: Batch systems prioritize throughput; simple FCFS or non-preemptive SJF often work well.

Q104. What is the purpose of the `exec()` family of functions in Unix/Linux?
A) To create a new process
B) To replace the current process image with a new program
C) To terminate a process
D) To list running processes
Answer: B
Explanation: `exec()` loads and runs a new program within the context of the existing process.

Q105. Which part of an IP address identifies the specific network?
A) Host portion
B) Network portion
C) Port number
D) MAC address
Answer: B
Explanation: The network portion, determined by the subnet mask, identifies the network segment.

Q106. In SQL, what does `COUNT(*)` return?
A) The number of columns in a table
B) The total number of rows in a table (or result set)
C) The sum of values in a column
D) The average value in a column
Answer: B
Explanation: `COUNT(*)` counts all rows satisfying the query's conditions.

Q107. Which data structure is used to implement function call stacks?
A) Queue
B) Stack
C) Linked List
D) Heap
Answer: B
Explanation: The LIFO nature of a stack mirrors how function calls are made and returned.

Q108. What is the maximum value representable by an 8-bit unsigned integer?
A) 127
B) 128
C) 255
D) 256
Answer: C
Explanation: An 8-bit unsigned integer can represent values from 0 to 2^8 - 1 = 255.

Q109. Which software testing type involves testing the system under high load?
A) Unit Testing
B) Integration Testing
C) Performance Testing (Load Testing)
D) Usability Testing
Answer: C
Explanation: Load testing evaluates system behavior under expected or peak load conditions.

Q110. What does the 'git branch' command do?
A) Merges branches
B) Lists, creates, or deletes branches
C) Switches to a different branch
D) Clones a repository
Answer: B
Explanation: Used alone, it lists branches. With arguments, it can create or delete them.

Q111. Which component translates assembly language into machine code?
A) Compiler
B) Interpreter
C) Assembler
D) Linker
Answer: C
Explanation: An assembler performs a relatively direct translation from assembly mnemonics to binary machine instructions.

Q112. What is the main characteristic of Reinforcement Learning?
A) Learning from labeled data
B) Learning from unlabeled data
C) Learning through trial-and-error based on rewards and penalties
D) Learning by explicit rules
Answer: C
Explanation: An agent learns to take actions in an environment to maximize a cumulative reward signal.

Q113. Which sorting algorithm has the best average-case time complexity among the following simple sorts?
A) Bubble Sort
B) Selection Sort
C) Insertion Sort
D) They all have O(n^2) average complexity
Answer: D
Explanation: While Insertion Sort performs better on nearly sorted data, all three have an average-case time complexity of O(n^2).

Q114. What is the function of the `finally` block in exception handling?
A) To catch exceptions
B) To execute code that must run whether an exception occurs or not (e.g., cleanup)
C) To throw an exception
D) To define the start of exception handling
Answer: B
Explanation: Ensures critical cleanup code (like closing files) executes.

Q115. What is the hexadecimal equivalent of binary 1110?

B) D

D) F
Answer: C
Explanation: 1110 (binary) = (1*8) + (1*4) + (1*2) + (0*1) = 14 (decimal) = E (hexadecimal).
